#define MaxWavePoints
 32768
// maximum number of samples per channel
#define
SamplePeriod 
1
// sampling period [10us]
#define
SendStatus
 
0x0500
// command codes for changing data on the status channel
#define
SendRealPos 
0x0501
#define
SendStatus2 
0x0512
#define
SendGalvoTemp 
0x0514
#define
SendHeadTemp 
0x0515
#define
SendAGC
 0x0516
#define
SendVccDSP 
0x0517
#define
SendVccDSPIO 
0x0518
#define
SendVccANA
 0x0519
#define
SendVccADC 
0x051A
#define
HeadA
 1
#define
XAxis
 1
#define
YAxis 
2
#define
StatusAX
 1
#define
StatusAY
 2
void delay(void)
// 100us delay
{
for (short i=0; i<10; i++)
z_out(0);
// dummy control function generates a 10us delay
}
void main(void)
{
long 
i;
short
ErrorCode;
unsigned short 
WavePoints;
short 
Ch1[MaxWavePoints], Ch2[MaxWavePoints];
// Initialize: load DSP Program File and correction file 
ErrorCode = load_program_file("RTC4D2.HEX");
if(ErrorCode) {
printf(DSP Program File loading error #%d\n",ErrorCode);
return;
}
ErrorCode = load_correction_file("Cor_1to1.ctb",
1,
// table; #1 is used by default
1.0, 1.0,
// scaling factor
0.0,
// rotation in degrees, counterclockwise
0.0, 0.0);
// offset in bits
if(ErrorCode) {
printf("Correction file loading error #%d\n",ErrorCode);
return;
}
// get some status information from the head
control_command(HeadA, XAxis, SendGalvoTemp);
// send X galvo temp on X status channel
control_command(HeadA, YAxis, SendGalvoTemp);
// send Y galvo temp on Y status channel
delay();
// wait until command is transfered to the head, executed and new status data is updated
printf("Temperature X-Galvo: %4.1f degrees centigrade\n",0.1*get_value(StatusAX));
// read X status channel
printf("Temperature Y-Galvo: %4.1f degrees centigrade\n",0.1*get_value(StatusAY));
// 1bit = 0.1 degree
// display AGC voltage of each galvo
control_command(HeadA, XAxis, SendAGC);
control_command(HeadA, YAxis, SendAGC);
delay();
printf("AGC Voltage X-Galvo: %5.2f Volts\n",0.01*get_value(StatusAX));
// 1bit = 10mV
printf("AGC Voltage Y-Galvo: %5.2f Volts\n",0.01*get_value(StatusAY));
// display internal status information
control_command(HeadA, XAxis, SendStatus2);
control_command(HeadA, YAxis, SendStatus2);
delay();
printf("Status2 x-Axis: %hX\n",get_value(StatusAX));
printf("Status2 y-Axis: %hX\n",get_value(StatusAY));

11.4 RTC4-Command Set
The commands are in alphabetical order. 
• RTC4 Ethernet Board-specific RTC4 commands 
can be found in Chapter 16.6.2, “Command Set 
for the RTC4 Ethernet Board”, Page 238. 
List Command
arc_abs
Function
Marking along the specified circular arc starting at the current position.
Parameters
x,y
Absolute coordinates of the arc center. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
angle
Arc angle in ° [–360.0°…+360.0°]. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Positive angle values correspond to clockwise angles.
Integration
Pascal:
arc_abs(x,y: smallint; angle: double);
C:
void arc_abs(short x, short y, double angle);
Basic:
arc_abs(ByVal x%, ByVal y%, ByVal angle#)
Comments
• The maximum allowed arc radius (in bits) is 32767.
• The mark speed is set by set_mark_speed.
• The laser is turned on at the beginning of the command after a LaserOn Delay. 
• If another arc[*] Command or mark[*] Command follows, a Polygon Delay is inserted, 
and the laser stays on. Otherwise a Mark Delay is inserted and the laser is turned off 
after a LaserOff Delay.
• See Chapter 4.2, “Scan Head and Laser Control”, Page 28, for further details.
References
set_mark_speed, set_scanner_delays, arc_rel

[p.118]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
118
innovators for industry
List Command
arc_rel
Function
Marking along the specified circular arc starting at the current position.
Parameters
dx,dy
Relative coordinates of the arc center. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
angle
Arc angle in ° [–360.0°…+360.0°]. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Positive angle values correspond to clockwise angles.
Integration
Pascal:
arc_rel(dx,dy: smallint; angle: double);
C:
void arc_rel(short dx, short dy, double angle);
Basic:
arc_rel(ByVal dx%, ByVal dy%, ByVal angle#)
Comments
• The arc center coordinates are relative to the current position.
• The maximum value for the absolute arc center coordinates is ±32767 bits.
• The mark speed is set by set_mark_speed.
• The laser is turned on at the beginning of the command after a LaserOn Delay. 
• If another arc[*] Command or mark[*] Command follows, a Polygon Delay is inserted, 
and the laser stays on. Otherwise a Mark Delay is inserted and the laser is turned off 
after a LaserOff Delay.
• See also Chapter 4.2, “Scan Head and Laser Control”, Page 28.
References
set_mark_speed, set_scanner_delays, arc_abs

[p.119]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
119
innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
auto_cal
Function
Starts or stops automatic self-calibration or re-calibrates the scan head.
Requires a scan head with automatic self-calibration option, see Chapter 5.9, “Automatic 
Self-Calibration”, Page 74.
Parameters
head
= 1:
Calibration of scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
= 2:
Calibration of scan system at 2nd scan head connector. 
command
Control parameter. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
= 0:Get reference values for subsequent calibration routines.
= 1:Perform calibration routine.
= 2:Turn off compensation.
Result
Error code. As a signed 16-bit value. 
0
No error.
1
Self-calibration sensor not found.
2
Deviations during a measurement cycle are too large.
3
The command cannot be executed because a list is executing at the moment.
4
Reference data not found.
5
Calibration error (error during calibration or error in reference data).
6
Parameter error.
7
Status error (error during data retransmission).
8
Inconsistent search algorithms (DLL file and HEX file do not have the same 
search algorithm version). 
Integration
Pascal:
function auto_cal(head, command: word): smallint;
C:
short auto_cal(unsigned short head, unsigned short command);
Basic:
function auto_cal(ByVal head%, ByVal command%)%
Comments
• auto_cal can only be used in combination with a scan head equipped with sensors for 
automatic self-calibration.
• auto_cal is not executed if a list is executing at the moment.
• auto_cal(…, 0) detects the current sensor positions and stores them as reference values 
for subsequent calibration routines. This should be performed under controlled, 
constant environmental conditions. The scan head must be at operating temperature, 
that is, the warm-up time should be at least 15 minutes.
The sensor positions are determined during a cycle of several measurements. If the 
deviations between the individual measurements are too large (maximum – minimum 
> 5 bits), the measurement stops and an error (error code 2) is returned. After 
successful determination of the reference values, the results are stored in non-volatile 
memory on the RTC4 board. This way, the values are not lost when the system is shut 
down.

[p.120]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
120
innovators for industry
Comments
(cont’d) 
• auto_cal(…, 1) performs a new calibration of the scan head, that is, 
compares the current sensor positions with the reference values and calculates suitable 
compensation values (for gain and offset) for each scanner. 
The resulting compensation is applied to all subsequent vector outputs, until 
auto_cal(…, 1) is called again or the compensation is turned off by auto_cal(…, 2).
• To compensate possible drift of the scanners, auto_cal(…, 1) should be called regularly 
during operation. The calibration routine takes about 5 seconds (depending on the 
amount of drift), the initial determination of the reference values ( auto_cal(…, 0) ) 
takes about 30…50 seconds.
• After initialization of the RTC4, or after a reset, the compensation is turned off.
However, the previously determined reference values are still available.
• Upon HEX version 439 sensor type 2 is supported.
Ctrl Command
auto_cal
Ctrl Command
auto_change
Function
Activates an automatic list change.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure auto_change;
C:
void auto_change(void);
Basic:
sub auto_change()
Comments
• auto_change should only be used when working with two lists (up to 4000 commands 
each). auto_change should only be used if a list is currently executing, or if it has 
already executed. Additionally, the other list should have already been loaded and 
closed.
• With automatic list changing activated, the next list starts automatically after the 
current list is finished.
• For each subsequent list, use a separate auto_change call.
• The current status of both lists can be read by get_status or read_status.
• See Chapter 4.1.3, “Automatic List Handling”, Page 25.
References
get_status, read_status

List 
Command
clear_io_cond_list
Function
Clears the bits of the 16-bit digital output port that are set (=1) in mask_clear, 
if the current IOvalue at the digital input port meets the following condition:
((IOvalue AND mask_1) = mask_1) AND (((not IOvalue) AND mask_0) = mask_0)
(that is, the bits specified in mask_1 must be 1 and the bits specified in mask_0 must be 0).
Parameters
mask_1, 
mask_0,
mask_clear
Masks. 
Each: As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure clear_io_cond_list(mask_1, mask_0, mask_clear: word);
C:
void clear_io_cond_list(unsigned short mask_1, unsigned short mask_0, 
unsigned short mask_clear);
Basic:
sub clear_io_cond_list(ByVal mask_1%, ByVal mask_0%, ByVal mask_clear%)
Comments
• clear_io_cond_list affects only those bits of the output port that are set (=1) in the 
parameter mask_clear.
Examples 
(Pascal)
• Clear Bit #4 of the output port (DIGITAL_OUT4), if Bit #0 of the input port 
(DIGITAL_IN0) is HIGH and Bit #1 to Bit #3 (DIGTAL_IN1…3) of the input port are LOW:
clear_io_cond_list($0001, $000E, $0010)
• always clear Bit #15 of the output port (and leave the other bits unchanged):
clear_io_cond_list(0, 0, $8000)
References
set_io_cond_list, get_io_status

Ctrl Command control_command 
Function 
Sends a control command. Whether and how the addressed scan system reacts depends 
on its properties (among other things, the scan system firmware). See also Comments, 
Page 123. 
Parameters 
head 
Scan head connector number of the RTC control board. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed values: 
= 1:
The scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
= 2:
The scan system at 2nd scan head connector. 
axis 
Number of the axis. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed values: 
= 1:
x axis (STATUS channel, Galvanometer scanner 2). 
= 2:
y axis (STATUS1 channel, Galvanometer scanner 1). 
= 3:
z axis. 
data 
Command code with optional parameter. See Chapter 18, “Appendix C: 
iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands and Signals Transmitted to 
RTC Control Boards”, Page 273. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
• CodeHIGH
The more significant data byte (Bit #8…Bit #15). Represents a command 
code. 
Presented as hexadecimal number in Chapter 18, “Appendix C: 
iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands and Signals Transmitted to 
RTC Control Boards”, Page 273. 
• CodeLOW
The less significant data byte (Bit #0…Bit #7). Represents an optional 
parameter. 
Presented as hexadecimal number in Chapter 18, “Appendix C: 
iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands and Signals Transmitted to 
RTC Control Boards”, Page 273. 
Example: By data = 0501H, that is, CodeHIGH = 05 (SetMode) and CodeLOW = 01 
the actual position is set as the data type to be transmitted. 
Integration 
Pascal:
procedure control_command(head, axis, data: word); 
C:
void control_command(unsigned short head, unsigned short axis, unsigned 
short data); 
Basic:
sub control_command(ByVal head As Integer, ByVal axis As Integer, ByVal 
data As Integer)

[p.123]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
123
innovators for industry
Comments 
• control_command can only be used with iDRIVE scan systems (see Glossary entry on 
page 14). 
• Conventional scan systems without iDRIVE technology ignore control_command. 
• With invalid values of head and/or axis, control_command is not executed.
• Command code data is transmitted to the scan system instead of the usual position 
data. Therefore, the corresponding galvanometer scanner Microstep is omitted, if 
control_command is called during execution of a list. 
References
get_value, get_head_status, set_trigger, get_waveform 
Ctrl Command control_command

Ctrl Command
disable_laser
Function
Deactivates the laser control of the RTC4.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure disable_laser;
C:
void disable_laser(void);
Basic:
sub disable_laser()
Comments
• disable_laser disables the laser signals LASER1, LASER2 and LASERON. That means 
pins (1), (2) (LASERON) and (3) of the 9-pin laser connector and pins (19) and (22) of 
the LASER EXTENSION socket connector then are static.
In case pin (2) of the 9-pin laser connector is configured as signal ANALOG OUT2, the 
command disable_laser does not have an effect on pin (2).
• Use enable_laser to re-enable the laser control.
• get_startstop_info (Bit #9) provides information about the current status of the laser 
control.
• After initialization of the RTC4 the laser control is active.
References
enable_laser, get_startstop_info
Ctrl Command
dsp_start
Function
Software Reset of the RTC4. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure dsp_start;
C:
void dsp_start(void);
Basic:
sub dsp_start()
Comments
• dsp_start is not needed for normal operation. The DSP starts automatically after the 
DSP Program File is loaded by load_program_file. 
• dsp_start causes a Software Reset of the RTC4. This means all parameters are reset to 
their default values. The laser focus is positioned in the center of the Image Field at the 
point (0|0). Previously loaded correction files and DSP Program Files remain in the RTC4 
memory, but the select_cor_table settings are reset to default. 
• After execution of dsp_start, the laser control is active.
References
load_program_file, enable_laser
Ctrl Command
enable_laser
Function
Activates the laser control of the RTC4.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure enable_laser;
C:
void enable_laser(void);
Basic:
sub enable_laser()
Comments
• enable_laser re-enables the laser signals LASER1, LASER2 and LASERON at the 9-pin 
laser connector and at the LASER EXTENSION socket connector.
• get_startstop_info provides information about the current status of the laser control. 
(Bit #9)
• After initialization of the RTC4, the laser control is active.
References
disable_laser, get_startstop_info

Ctrl Command
execute_at_pointer
Function
Starts list execution at the specified address in the RTC4 list buffer.
See also Chapter 5.6, “Structured Programming”, Page 65.
Parameter
pointer
Address of the first list command to be executed. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed range: [0…7999]. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure execute_at_pointer(pointer: word);
C:
void execute_at_pointer(unsigned short pointer);
Basic:
sub execute_at_pointer(ByVal pointer%)
Comments
• execute_at_pointer can be used instead of execute_list. 
For instance, execute_at_pointer(0) is the same as execute_list(1), 
execute_at_pointer(4000) is the same as execute_list(2). 
However, execution can be started at any other position in the list buffer as well.
• Notice! If the end of the list buffer is reached, the RTC4 continues at the address zero. 
• Execution stops when set_end_of_list is encountered.
• execute_at_pointer is ignored if a list is executing at the moment.
References
set_input_pointer, get_input_pointer
Ctrl Command
execute_list
Function
Starts execution of list 1 or list 2.
Parameter
list_no
Number of the list to be executed (1 or 2).
Integration
Pascal:
procedure execute_list(list_no: word);
C:
void execute_list(unsigned short list_no);
Basic:
sub execute_list(ByVal list_no%)
Comments
• execute_list_1 and execute_list_2 (with no parameters) 
can be used alternatively.
• Execution stops when set_end_of_list is encountered.
• During execution of a particular list, the other list can be loaded. However, that other 
list must not be started by execute_list until the current list execution is finished. 
(execute_list is ignored if a list is executing at the moment.) 
See also “List Handling and Status”, Page 25.
• Use the command get_status to determine the current status of execution.
References
get_status, execute_at_pointer

Ctrl Command
get_head_status
Function
Returns the XY2-100 status word from the specified scan head connector.
Parameter
head
= 1:
Scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
= 2:
Scan system at 2nd scan head connector. 
Integration
Pascal:
function get_head_status(head: word): word;
C:
unsigned short get_head_status(unsigned short head);
Basic:
function get_head_status(ByVal head%)%
Result
XY2-100 status word. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Bit #15
(MSB)
Power Status, 1 = OK.
Bit #14
Temperature Status, 1 = OK.
Bit #13
Reserved.
Bit #12
Position Acknowledge Y, 1 = OK.
Bit #11
Position Acknowledge X, 1 = OK.
Bit #10
Reserved.
Bit #9
0.
Bit #8
1.
Bit #7
…
Bit #0
Identical to Bit #15…Bit #8. 
Comments
• See Chapter 5.3, “Using Two Different Correction Files”, Page 62 for information about 
using two scan heads.
• It is also important to consider all the status signal information described in your 
scan system operating manual.
• With iDRIVE scan systems (see Glossary entry on page 14): 
– get_head_status only returns meaningful return values, if the XY2-100 status word 
has been selected (by control_command at the scan system) to be transmitted 
– The Position Acknowledge signals of the x axis and y axis are logically AND-
connected and only returned as a common signal at Bit #3, 4, 11, 12 (here, in 
addition, the Position Acknowledge signals of the x axis and y axis can be separately 
read out by control_command with data = 0528H at flag Bit #12) 
– After a reset or power-up, it can take around 5 seconds before valid data starts being 
returned from the scan system. This can be verified by monitoring Bit #8 and Bit #9: 
Bit #8 = 1 and Bit #9 = 0 (only) if transmission is correct. 
References
get_status, read_status, set_piso_control

Status signal.

(LSB) 
= 1:

= 1:

get_status
Function
Returns the current status of list execution.
Result
busy
true ( 0 ) : a list is executing at the moment
false ( = 0 ) : no list is executing at the moment
position
Pointer to the command which is executing at the moment 
0  position  7999.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure get_status(var busy: wordbool, var position: word);
C:
void get_status(unsigned short *busy, unsigned short *position);
Basic:
sub get_status(busy%, position%)
Comments
• If position < 4000, list 1 is executing at the moment, otherwise list 2.
• If busy = false, the variable pointer contains the position of the last command that was 
executed (usually set_end_of_list).
• In Pascal the variable busy can alternatively be of the type boolean.
• The busy signal is also available at pin (13) of the MARKING ON THE FLY connector 
(TTL level; a HIGH level indicates that a list is executing at the moment).
• The busy parameter is set to false ( = 0 ), if the list processing has been finished or has 
been stopped at a wait marker. 
See also comments at set_wait and release_wait.
References
read_status, get_head_status, set_wait, release_wait

[p.138]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
138
innovators for industry
Result 
Current value of the specified signal. 
As a signed 16-bit value. 
Integration 
Pascal:
function get_value(signal: word): smallint; 
C:
short get_value(unsigned short signal); 
Basic:
function get_value (ByVal signal As Integer) As Integer 
Comments 
• The type of scan system being used determines which status signals are generated and 
returned by the status channels. Specific information can be found in your scan system 
manual. 
• For scan systems with only one status channel, the status signals are only readable if 
signal = 1 or signal = 4. 
• Coordinate Transformations defined by set_matrix, set_matrix_list, set_offset or 
set_offset_list are already reflected in the SampleX, SampleY and SampleZ Cartesian 
output values. 
• The SampleAX_Corr…SampleBZ_Corr output values are the (digital) output values 
actually transmitted from the RTC4 to the scan system. The RTC4 computes these values 
while taking into account the SampleX, SampleY, SampleZ output values as well as the 
selected correction file. 
• To observe the specified signal over a long time period, use set_trigger to start a 
corresponding measurement session. 
References

143
innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
goto_xy
Function
Direct jump to the specified position.
Parameters
xpos, 
ypos
Coordinates of the jump position. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure goto_xy(xpos, ypos: smallint);
C:
void goto_xy(short xpos, short ypos);
Basic:
sub goto_xy(ByVal xpos%, ByVal ypos%)
Comments
• With DSP Program Files RTC4D2.HEX V2.417 / RTC4D3.HEX V3.417, the jump speed is 
set by set_jump_speed. With older DSP Program File versions, goto_xy jumps are 
always be executed at a speed of 50,000 bits/ms.
• Usually scan systems are optimized for scanning vectors (not for jumps). Therefore, 
after executing a jump by the goto_xy command with a high jump speed, a large 
overshoot may occur. Then – depending on the jump distance – the set positions may 
be reached only after a longer settling time. Therefore, an appropriate low jump speed 
should be previously set by set_jump_speed. As with DSP Program Files 
RTC4D2.HEX V2.416 / RTC4D3.HEX V3.416, the jump speed is always set to maximum 
value of 50000 bits / ms, jumps should be realized by the list commands jump_abs or 
jump_rel with this DSP Program File versions.
• goto_xy is ignored if a list is executing at the moment.
• goto_xy is not executed, if an external stop signal (/STOP or /STOP2) is present.
• Image Field correction is applied.
• If an coordinate transformation is defined by set_matrix / set_offset, it is applied to 
the specified vector.
References
get_xy_pos, set_jump_speed, jump_abs, jump_rel

Ctrl Command
home_position
Function
Activates the home jump mode and defines the home position.
Parameters
xhome, 
yhome
Coordinates of the home position. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure home_position (xhome, yhome: smallint);
C:
void home_position (short xhome, short yhome);
Basic:
sub home_position (ByVal xhome%, ByVal yhome%)
Comments
• home_position is intended for a laser system that does not allow fast switching of the 
laser. After calling home_position, the laser focus moves to the specified home 
position whenever no list is executing.
• A home jump is also executed, if list execution is stopped by stop_execution but not if 
list execution is stopped by an external stop signal.
• At the beginning of the next list, the laser focus automatically jumps to the start point 
of the first list vector. The RTC2 command field_jump is no longer needed.
• A beam dump should be placed in the home position.
• The home jump mode is deactivated by home_position(0, 0).
References
–

laser_on_list
Function
Turns on the laser for a specified time interval.
Parameter
delay 
Time interval. In bits. As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
1 bit equals 10 µs.
Allowed range: 0 delay 65500. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure laser_on_list(delay: word);
C:
void laser_on_list(unsigned short delay);
Basic:
sub laser_on_list(ByVal delay%)
Comments
• While the laser is turned on, the set position of the scanners is not changed. The next 
list command is executed when the programmed time interval has passed.
• The current settings for the Laser Delays are applied:
– At the beginning of the programmed time interval, the laser turns on after a
LaserOn Delay.
– At the end of the time interval, the laser turns off with the corresponding 
LaserOff Delay.
• laser_on_list is useful for marking separate dots.

List Command
list_call_cond
Function
Conditional subroutine call: During execution of a list, this command causes a jump to a 
subroutine at the specified list buffer address [0…7999], if the current IOvalue at the 16-bit 
digital input port meets the following condition:
((IOvalue AND mask_1) = mask_1) AND (((not IOvalue) AND mask_0) = mask_0)
(that is, the bits specified in mask_1 must be 1 and the bits specified in mask_0 must be 0).
Parameters
mask_1, 
mask_0
Masks. As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
address
Jump address [0…7999]. As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
list_call_cond(mask_1, mask_0, address: word);
C:
void list_call_cond(unsigned short mask_1, unsigned short mask_0, 
unsigned short address);
Basic:
sub list_call_cond(ByVal mask_1%, ByVal mask_0%, ByVal address%)
Comments
• The subroutine must be terminated by list_return.
See Chapter 5.6, “Structured Programming”, Page 65.
• See also Chapter 5.6.5, “Programming Examples (Pascal)”, Page 66, sample #(3).
References
list_call, list_return
List Command
list_jump_cond
Function
Conditional list jump: During execution of a list, this command causes a jump to the 
specified list buffer address [0…7999], if the current IOvalue at the 16-bit digital input port 
meets the following condition:
((IOvalue AND mask_1) = mask_1) AND (((not IOvalue) AND mask_0) = mask_0)
(that is, the bits specified in mask_1 must be 1 and the bits specified in mask_0 must be 0).
Parameters
mask_1, 
mask_0
Masks. As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
address
Jump address [0…7999]. As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
list_jump_cond(mask_1, mask_0, address: word);
C:
void list_jump_cond(unsigned short mask_1, unsigned short mask_0, 
unsigned short address);
Basic:
sub list_jump_cond(ByVal mask_1%, ByVal mask_0%, ByVal address%)
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.6, “Structured Programming”, Page 65.
Examples 
(Pascal)
• Wait until Bit #3 of the input port turns HIGH (= loop while the bit is LOW):
list_jump_cond(0, $0008, get_input_pointer);
• Skip the next two list commands if the state of the input port is xxxx xxxx xxxx 0110 :
list_jump_cond(6, 9, get_input_pointer + 3);
• See also Chapter 5.6.5, “Programming Examples (Pascal)”, Page 66.

Command
load_correction_file
Function
Loads the specified field correction file into RTC4 memory (as table #1 or #2) and performs 
additional scaling, rotation and translation of the correction file.
Parameters
FileName
Name of the correction file. 
As a pointer to a null-terminated ANSI string. 
cor_table
Determines whether the file shall be stored as correction table #1 or #2. 
See select_cor_table.
kx, ky
Gain values for scaling the correction table. 
Allowed range: [–1.2…–0.8, +0.8…+1.2].
phi
Rotational angle in degrees.
Allowed values: [–10°…+10°] + i × 90°; i integer.
Positive angles: rotation is counterclockwise.
x_offset, 
y_offset
Additional offset. In bits. 
Allowed range: [–30000…+30000].

[p.154]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
154
innovators for industry
Result
Error code. As a signed 16-bit value. 
Value
Description.
0
Success.
3
File error.
4
Verify error.
8
System driver not found, or the system driver is locked by another 
application (access rights assigned to another application).
10
Parameter error.
11
RTC4 not found.
12
A 3D correction file could not be loaded, because the Option “3D” is not 
installed. See Chapter 7, “Options”, Page 93.
14
Ethernet error. See eth_get_last_error. 
Integration
Pascal:
function load_correction_file(FileName: pchar; cor_table: smallint; kx, 
ky, phi, x_offset, y_offset: double): smallint;
C:
short load_correction_file(const char* FileName, short cor_table, double 
kx, double ky, double phi, double x_offset, double y_offset);
Basic:
function load_correction_file(ByVal FileName$, ByVal cor_table%, ByVal 
kx#, ByVal ky#, ByVal phi#, ByVal x_offset#, ByVal y_offset#)%
Comments
• Recommendation on the command sequence within the application source code: load 
the DSP Program File first (load_program_file), then the correction file 
(load_correction_file). 
See also Chapter 10.3, “Initializing the RTC4 PCIe Board”, Page 105.
• The RTC4 (only the RTC4 2D version) can store two different correction files at the same 
time, for example, for use in a double scan head configuration. The files must be 
assigned to the two scan heads by select_cor_table. 
See also Chapter 5.3, “Using Two Different Correction Files”, Page 62.
• To compensate possible misalignment or to align the Image Fields of the two 
scan heads precisely, each correction file can be scaled, rotated and translated (shifted) 
when it is loaded into the RTC4.
• The parameters kx, ky, phi, x_offset and y_offset have to be specified. If no additional 
transformation is required, the parameters must be set to (…, …, 1, 1, 0, 0, 0).
• By setting the gain factor kx or ky to a negative value, the corresponding axis is flipped.
• Modification of 3D correction files is only reliable for Z = 0. For other z values and 
parameters other than (…, …, 1, 1, 0, 0, 0), the RTC4 calculates output values which 
may deviate from the expected values.
References
select_cor_table, load_program_file
Ctrl 
Command
load_correction_file

[p.155]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US

155
innovators for industry
 
Ctrl Command
load_program_file
Function
Loads the specified DSP Program File into RTC4 memory.
Parameter
FileName
Name of the DSP Program File. 
As a pointer to a null-terminated ANSI string. 
Result
Error code. As a signed 16-bit value. 
Value
Description
0
Success.
3
File error.
4
Verify error.
6
Number of bytes in Intel hex file is odd.
7
Checksum error in Intel hex file.
8
System driver not found, or the system driver is locked by another application 
(access rights assigned to another application).
9
DSP Program File not complete.
11
RTC4 not found. 
14 
Ethernet error. See eth_get_last_error. 
15 
Applicable only to V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards: the board has not been 
previously acquired. 
Integration
Pascal:
function load_program_file(FileName: pchar): smallint;
C:
short load_program_file(const char* FileName);
Basic:
function load_program_file(ByVal FileName$)%
Comments
• Recommendation on the command sequence within the application source code: load 
the DSP Program File first (load_program_file), then the correction file 
(load_correction_file). See also Chapter 10.3, “Initializing the RTC4 PCIe Board”, 
Page 105.
• The filename extension for DSP Program Files is *.HEX.
• load_program_file resets the RTC4. This means all parameters are reset to their default 
values. The laser focus is positioned in the center of the Image Field at the point (0|0). 
If any correction file(s) were loaded previously, they remain in RTC4 memory, but the 
select_cor_table settings are reset to default.
• After execution of load_program_file, the laser control is active.
References
load_correction_file, dsp_start

Ctrl Command
load_varpolydelay
Function
Loads a table for the “Variable Polygon Delay” into the RTC4.
See Section ”User-defined “Variable Polygon Delays””, Page 39.
Parameters
STBFileName
Name of the data file (with extension *.STB). 
As a pointer to a null-terminated ANSI string. 
A data file can contain one or more tables.
TableNo
Specifies which table in the data file shall be used.
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
The parameter TableNo must be identical with extension X of the command 
[VarPolyTableX] which denotes the desired table.
Result
Error code. 
As a signed 16-bit value. 
Value
Description
–1
Success. The absolute value of the error code is equal to the number of 
valid data points found in the table. Invalid entries are ignored. 
See Section ”User-defined “Variable Polygon Delays””, Page 39.
4
Verify error.
8
System driver not found, or the system driver is locked by another 
application.
10
Parameter error.
11
RTC4 not found.
13
The specified table number was not found in the file; or the file was not 
found.
14
Ethernet error. See eth_get_last_error. 
Integration
Pascal:
function load_varpolydelay (STBFileName: pchar, TableNo: word): smallint;
C:
short load_varpolydelay (const char* STBFileName, unsigned short 
TableNo);
Basic:
function load_varpolydelay (ByVal STBFileName$, ByVal TableNo%)%
Comments
• The table contains a number of data points for the user-defined “Variable 
Polygon Delay”, see Section ”User-defined “Variable Polygon Delays””, Page 39. 
When loading the table, the RTC4 determines suitable values for the entire 
range of angles by linear interpolation. 
• load_varpolydelay overwrites any previously loaded table for the “Variable 
Polygon Delay”. 
• After loading a DSP Program File by load_program_file, or after a Software Reset by 
dsp_start, the RTC4 uses the internal (default) table for the “Variable Polygon Delay”, 
see Figure 9. That means the command load_varpolydelay is only needed if a different 
table should be used.
• To return to the internal Polygon Delay table (after a different table has been used), 
either load_program_file or dsp_start must be called. 
References
load_program_file, set_delay_mode

Ctrl Command
load_z_table 
Function
Generates a new correction table for the z-output values. 
Prerequisite 
Enabled Option “3D”. 
Parameters
A 
B 
C 
Coefficients of the parabolic function Z = A + Bl +Cl2 which is used for 
calculating the z-output table. 
Each: As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Integration
Pascal:
function load_z_table(A, B, C: double): smallint; 
C:
short load_z_table(double A, double B, double C); 
Basic:
function load_z_table(ByVal A#, ByVal B#, ByVal C#)% 
Result
Error status. 
As a signed 16-bit value. 
0
No error. 
4
Verify error. 
8
Driver not found, or the driver is locked by another application. 
10
Parameter error. 
11
RTC not found. 
12
Option “3D” not installed. 
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.10, “3D Functionality”, Page 75. 
• load_z_table is only needed for re-calibrating the z axis in a 3D scan system. 
See Chapter 5.10.7 “Calibrating z Axes”, Page 78. 
• The correction table is calculated using the function Z = A + Bl +Cl2. 
l is the relative focus shift between the points (x|y|z) and (0|0|0). 
• The z output values should be in the range – 32,768…+32,767 (signed 16-bit values).
In particular the coefficients A, B, C and the focus shift l can be negative. 
• load_z_table should be called directly after load_correction_file, since 
load_correction_file resets the z-output table to the default values.

get_z_distance

mark_abs
Function
Marking along a straight line from the current position to the specified position.
Parameters
xval, 
yval
Absolute coordinates of the vector end point. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure mark_abs(xval, yval: smallint);
C:
void mark_abs(short xval, short yval);
Basic:
sub mark_abs(ByVal xval%, ByVal yval%)
Comments
• The mark speed is set by set_mark_speed.
• The laser is turned on at the beginning of the command after a LaserOn Delay. 
• If another mark[*] Command or arc[*] Command follows, a Polygon Delay is inserted, 
and the laser stays on. Otherwise a Mark Delay is inserted and the laser is turned off 
after a LaserOff Delay.
• If a marking vector is followed by a zero jump or marking vector or a zero 
arc[*] Command, then the MarkDelay is not executed.
• See also Chapter 4.2, “Scan Head and Laser Control”, Page 28.

select_cor_table
Function
Assigns the previously loaded correction tables #1 and #2 to the scan head control ports.
Parameters
head_a
= 0:
Turns off the signals for scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
= 1:
Assigns correction table #1 to scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
= 2:
Assigns correction table #2 to scan system at 1st scan head connector. 
head_b
= 0:
Turns off the signals for scan system at 2nd scan head connector. 
= 1:
Assigns correction table #1 to scan system at 2nd scan head 
connector. 
= 2:
Assigns correction table #2 to scan system at 2nd scan head 
connector. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure select_cor_table(head_a, head_b: word);
C:
void select_cor_table(unsigned short head_a, unsigned short head_b);
Basic:
sub select_cor_table(ByVal head_a%, ByVal head_b%)
Comments
• In a double scan head system 
– correction table #1 is used for scan system at 1st scan head connector 
– correction table #2 is used for scan system at 2nd scan head connector 
that is, select_cor_table(1,2) 
• However, each of the two correction tables can be assigned to any of the two scan head 
control ports. This allows, for example, to switch rapidly between two correction files 
for one scan head, for example, one for a pointer laser and one for the main laser with 
a different wavelength. (Use select_cor_table(1,0) and select_cor_table(2,0) to 
switch from one file to the other.)
• The default setting is (1,0), that is, 
– correction table #1 is used for scan system at 1st scan head connector, 
– output signals for scan system at 2nd scan head connector are turned off 
See also Chapter 5.3, “Using Two Different Correction Files”, Page 62.
• An RTC4 with Option “3D” can store only one correction file. 
References
load_correction_file

select_rtc

Defines the active RTC4 board in a multi-board system.

Parameter

Board number (see below). 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure select_rtc(card_no: word); 
C:
void select_rtc(unsigned short card_no); 
Basic:
sub select_rtc(ByVal card_no As Integer) As Integer 
Comments
• card_no expects a board number from the DLL-internal RTC4 board management. 
With RTC4 Ethernet Boards, it must have been previously assigned by assign_rtc or 
assign_rtc_by_ip. 
• RTC4ethDLL.dll contains a number of commands both 
– with n_ prefix (multi-board commands) and 
– without n_ prefix (non-multi-board commands). 
Multi-board commands expect the user-defined card number as first parameter. 
Thus, the RTC4 board that is to execute the command is specified directly. 
Alternatively, an active RTC4 board can be defined globally by select_rtc. All 
subsequent non-multi-board commands are then forwarded to this active RTC4 board. 
If this RTC4 board has not been explicitly taken over before, select_rtc tries to do so 
implicitly. 
• See also Chapter 16.4.1, “Compatibility Mode”, Page 233.

170
innovators for industry
Ctrl 
Command
set_delay_mode
Function 
Turns the “Variable Polygon Delays” mode and the “Variable Jump Delays“ mode on (off). 
Parameters 
varpoly 
> 0 
= 0 
Enables “Variable Polygon Delays” mode.
Disables “Variable Polygon Delays” mode. 
Default setting. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
directmove3d 
> 0
= 0
directmove3d affects only 3D-user programs. 
x value, y value, z value are changed directly (linearly) 
to their end values during a jump. 
While x value, y value are changed linearly to their 
end values during a jump, the z value is changed to 
its end-value in such a way that the focus is kept in 
one plane during the entire jump. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
edgelevel 
0…65500
1 bit equals 
10 µs
edgelevel defines a maximum “laser on“ time for the 
corners of a Polyline. If the Polygon Delay is longer 
than or equal to this value (because the angle  is 
close to 180°, for instance), the laser is turned off 
(after a LaserOff Delay) and a new Polyline is started. 
This can be useful for preventing burn-in effects. The 
edgelevel must be smaller than twice the set value for 
the Polygon Delay, otherwise it has no effect. See also 
Figure 9. To disable this feature, set edgelevel to 
65500 (default value). 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
MinJumpDelay 
0…32500
1 bit equals 
10 µs
Minimum Jump Delay for a jump vector of zero 
length, see Figure 6. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
JumpLengthLimit 
0…32500
Jump length limit. In bits. If the jump vector is shorter 
than this value, the Jump Delay is varied as shown in 
Figure 6. Otherwise the Jump Delay is constant.
JumpLengthLimit = 0 disables “Variable 
Jump Delays“ mode. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value.

172
innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
set_ext_start_delay 
Function
Defines a delay (counter pulses) to be inserted after each external /START signal (before the 
following list is started). 
Prerequisite 
Enabled Option Processing-on-the-fly. 
Parameters
delay 
See comments. 
As a signed 16-bit value.
encoder 
= 0:
Use ENCODER X. 
= 1:
Use ENCODER Y. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_ext_start_delay(delay, encoder: smallint);
C:
void set_ext_start_delay(short delay, short encoder);
Basic:
sub set_ext_start_delay(ByVal delay%, ByVal encoder%)
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.11, “Processing-on-the-fly Functionality”, Page 79. 
• set_ext_start_delay can be only used together with a real encoder (hardware encoder), 
not together with simulate_encoder. 
• A separate counter is used for the external start delay. When the RTC receives an 
external start signal, the counter is set to zero. Afterwards the pulses from the selected 
encoder are counted. When the counter reaches the value [delay × 16], the list is 
started (The list is started only, if no list is executing at the moment). 
• The encoder pulses are counted with sign, that is, depending on the direction of the 
motion. If the object moves in a negative direction, delay should be negative as well. 
• To specify the start position of the list to be executed, use set_extstartpos_list or 
select_list. 
• delay = 0 turns off the external start delay. 
References
simulate_ext_start, set_ext_start_delay_list, select_list, set_extstartpos_list, 
set_control_mode 
List Command

C:
void set_ext_start_delay_list(short delay, short encoder);
Basic:
sub set_ext_start_delay_list(ByVal delay%, ByVal encoder%)

• See also Chapter 5.11, “Processing-on-the-fly Functionality”, Page 79.

innovators for industry
List Command
set_extstartpos_list
Function
Defines the start position (list buffer address) of the list to be executed by the next external 
start signal.
Parameter
position
List pointer to the start address of the list [0…7999].
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_extstartpos_list(position: word);
C:
void set_extstartpos_list(unsigned short position);
Basic:
sub set_extstartpos_list(ByVal position%)
Comments
• set_extstartpos_list is a list command. When set_extstartpos_list is used within a list, 
set_extstartpos_list “links“ the current list to the next list.
• set_extstartpos_list(0) selects list 1. 
set_extstartpos_list(4000) selects list 2. 
However, any other position in the list buffer can be specified as well.
• The specified start address is used for all subsequent external starts until a new address 
is specified either by set_extstartpos_list or by select_list.
References
select_list, set_control_mode, simulate_ext_start

RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
175
innovators for industry
List Command
set_fly_rot 
Function
Sets the encoder resolution for ENCODER X and starts Processing-on-the-fly for 
compensation of a rotary motion. 
Prerequisite 
Enabled Option Processing-on-the-fly. 
Parameters
resolution 
Encoder pulses per revolution. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_fly_rot(var resolution: double);
C:
void set_fly_rot(double resolution);
Basic:
sub set_fly_rot(ByVal resolution#)
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.11, “Processing-on-the-fly Functionality”, Page 79. 
• When set_fly_rot is executed, the ENCODER X counter resets to zero. 
• After set_fly_rot executes, the x value and y value of the current output position are 
continuously corrected with respect to the current ENCODER X counter value. 
This correction is performed every 10 µs. 
• Before executing set_fly_rot, the rotation center must be defined by set_rot_center. 
• Use get_encoder to calibrate the encoder, that is, to determine the encoder resolution 
[in counts per revolution]. Note, that the number of counts per revolution is 4 times the 
number of encoder pulses per revolution, see Chapter , “Detecting the Motion of the 
Object”, Page 79. It might be necessary to correct the implied direction of motion by 
inverting the sign of the encoder resolution. 
• The encoder counters are signed 32-bit counters. Overflows will not be intercepted. 
• Use the fly_return to turn off Processing-on-the-fly correction and thereby define a 
new output position. 
• If the absolute value of the encoder resolution is < 100, then the Processing-on-the-fly 
correction is also turned off. The end point of the last transferred vector is then 
repeated without the correction. 
References
set_rot_center, get_encoder, fly_return

[p.176]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
176
innovators for industry
List Command
set_fly_x 
Function
Sets the Scaling Factor for ENCODER X and starts Processing-on-the-fly for compensation 
of a linear motion in the x direction. 
Prerequisite 
Enabled Option Processing-on-the-fly. 
Parameters 
kx 
Scaling factor [bits/count]. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_fly_x(var kx: double);
C:
void set_fly_x(double kx);
Basic:
sub set_fly_x(ByVal kx#)
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.11, “Processing-on-the-fly Functionality”, Page 79. 
• When set_fly_x is executed, the ENCODER X counter resets to zero. 
• After set_fly_x executes, the x value of the current output position is continuously 
corrected with respect to the current ENCODER X counter value. 
This correction is performed every 10 µs. 
• The encoder counters are signed 32-bit counters. Overflows will not be intercepted. 
• Use get_encoder to calibrate the encoder, that is, to determine the encoder increment 
[in counts per mm]. 
• The Scaling Factor must be specified in bits per count. For calculating the Scaling Factor 
see Scaling Factor, Page 81. It might be necessary to correct the implied direction of 
motion by inverting the sign of the Scaling Factor.

output position. 
• If the Scaling Factor is set to zero, then the Processing-on-the-fly correction is also 
turned off. The end point of the last transferred vector is then repeated without the 
correction.

innovators for industry
List Command
set_io_cond_list
Function
Set the bits of the 16-bit digital output port that are set (=1) in mask_set, 
if the current IOvalue at the digital input port meets the following condition:
((IOvalue AND mask_1) = mask_1) AND (((not IOvalue) AND mask_0) = mask_0)
(that is, the IOvalue’s bits specified in mask_1 must be 1 and the IOvalue’s bits specified in 
mask_0 must be 0).
Parameters
mask_1, 
mask_0,
mask_set
Masks. 
Each: As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_io_cond_list(mask_1, mask_0, mask_set: word);
C:
void set_io_cond_list(unsigned short mask_1, unsigned short mask_0, 
unsigned short mask_set);
Basic:
sub set_io_cond_list(ByVal mask_1%, ByVal mask_0%, ByVal mask_set%)
Comments
• set_io_cond_list affects only those bits of the output port that are set (=1) in the 
parameter mask_set.
Examples 
(Pascal)
• Set Bit #4 of the output port (DIGITAL_OUT4), if Bit #0 of the input port (DIGITAL_IN0) 
is HIGH and Bit #1 to Bit #3 (DIGTAL_IN1…3) of the input port are LOW: 
set_io_cond_list($0001, $000E, $0010)
• Always set Bit #15 of the output port (and leave the other bits unchanged):
set_io_cond_list(0, 0, $8000)
References
clear_io_cond_list, get_io_status
List Command
set_jump_speed
Function
Defines the jump speed for the subsequent Vector Commands. 
Parameter
jump_speed
Jump speed in bits per ms. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Allowed range: [1…50000]. 
Out-of-range values are clipped to the boundary values. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_jump_speed(jump_speed: double);
C:
void set_jump_speed(double jump_speed);
Basic:
sub set_jump_speed(ByVal jump_speed#)
Comments
• The command is written directly into the list.
• By default a jump speed of 100 bits per ms is preset.
• The specified jump speed (or the preset jump speed, if no other value has been 
specified) is used for all subsequent jump[*] Commands until a new value is specified.
• To obtain the actual jump speed v in the image plane (in meters per second), the 
specified speed value (in bits per ms) must be divided by the calibration factor K 
of the correction file (in bits per mm): 
vjump = jump_speed / K
References
jump_abs, jump_rel, set_mark_speed

set_max_counts
Function
Defines the maximum number of external list starts.
Parameter

Maximum number of external list starts. 
As a signed 32-bit value. 
Allowed range: 0  max_counts  2147483647.
Integration

C:
void set_max_counts(long max_counts);
Basic:
sub set_max_counts(ByVal max_counts&)
Comments
• If the parameter max_counts is set to 0, the maximum number of external start signals 
is unlimited.
• After a Software Reset of the RTC4 the parameter max_counts is set to 0.
• The counter can be read by get_counts.
• When the specified number of external start signals is reached, bit 0 of the 
control_mode register is set to zero. Thus no further external start signals are possible.
• To reset the counter, call set_control_mode.

List Command
set_pixel
Function
Defines the output parameters (laser pulse length and ANALOG OUT2 value) for one pixel 
in an image line. In addition, one of the four analog input ports of the I/O Extension Board 
for RTC3/RTC4 (Accessory) can be read during the output of the pixel (RTC4 with 
I/O Extension Board for RTC3/RTC4 (Accessory) only).
See also Chapter 5.7, “Pixel Output Mode”, Page 67.
Parameters
pulse_width
Laser output pulse length. 
1 bit equals 1/8 µs. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
da_value
Output value for the ANALOG OUT2 port of the RTC4 (10-bit resolution) 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
The upper 6 bits are ignored, the ANALOG OUT2 output port has a 10-bit 
resolution. 
ad_channel
Number of the ADC input channel to be read [0…4; 0 = none]. 
The RTC4 writes the obtained ADC result into the current list (at the 
position of the corresponding set_pixel command). The value can be read 
by read_pixel_ad after execution of the list.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_pixel(pulse_width, da_value, ad_channel: word);
C:
void set_pixel(unsigned short pulse_width, unsigned short da_value, 
unsigned short ad_channel);
Basic:
sub set_pixel(ByVal pulse_width%, ByVal da_value%, ByVal ad_channel%)
Comments
• Each image line must start with set_pixel_line.
• Each pixel in the image line is defined by one set_pixel call. The set_pixel calls must 
follow immediately after set_pixel_line. 
No other commands must be written into the list until the image line is completed.
References
set_pixel_line, read_pixel_ad

Switches to the pixel output mode, defines various pixel output parameters and marks the 
beginning of a pixel line. See also Chapter 5.7, “Pixel Output Mode”, Page 67. 
Parameters
pixel_mode
= 0:The laser focus “jumps“ from one pixel to the next.
= 1:The laser focus moves from one pixel to the next in small steps 
(Microsteps). See also Chapter 5.7, “Pixel Output Mode”, 
Page 67.
pixel_period
Pixel output period. 
1 bit equals 10 µs. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
dx, dy
Distance in the X and Y directions between adjacent pixels. In bits. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_pixel_line(pixel_mode, pixel_period: word; dx, dy: double);
C:
void set_pixel_line(unsigned short pixel_mode, unsigned short 
pixel_period, double dx, double dy);
Basic:
sub set_pixel_line(ByVal pixel_mode%, ByVal pixel_period%, ByVal dx#, 
ByVal dy#)
Comments
• Each image line must start with set_pixel_line. 
• set_pixel_line should be preceded by a jump[*] Command to the start point of the 
image line.
• set_pixel_line turns on the pixel output mode of the RTC4. 
The individual pixels of the image line are defined by set_pixel calls. 
The set_pixel calls must follow immediately after set_pixel_line. 
• The first subsequent command in the list which is not a set_pixel command turns off 
the pixel output mode.
• set_pixel_line requires two list entries in the list buffer memory. 
References
set_pixel

innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
set_softstart_level
Function
Sets the softstart values.
Parameters 
index
Index number of the softstart table value. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed range: 0…number. 
level
Voltage. 
Allowed range: 0…1023. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Value 0 corresponds to 0 V. 
Value 1023 corresponds to: 
– 2.50 V for jumper X3 Position 1-2 
– 10 V for jumper X3 Position 2-3 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_softstart_level (index, level: word);
C:
void set_softstart_level (unsigned short index, unsigned short level);
Basic:
sub set_softstart_level (ByVal index%, ByVal level%)
Comments
• set_softstart_level defines the level value for the pulse number index. 
set_softstart_level must be called separately for each individual level value.
• index must be in the range [0…1000], otherwise set_softstart_level is not executed.
• If index > number (number is defined by set_softstart_mode) then set_softstart_level 
is executed but the defined value is not used during softstart.
• Be sure to set as many softstart values as you defined by set_softstart_mode 
(unspecified softstart values have undefined contents).
• Softstart Mode is enabled by set_softstart_mode.
• level is restricted to 10 bits; higher bits are ignored.
• The set_softstart_mode command must be called before first-time set_softstart_level 
call. Otherwise, the specified value is not correctly converted to an analog value.
• Also observe the notes in Chapter 4.6.4, “Softstart Mode”, Page 53.
References
set_softstart_mode

set_softstart_mode
Function
Switches Softstart Mode on or off.
Parameters
Each: As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Parameter
Allowed Values
Description
mode
= 0
= 1, 11
= 2, 12
= 1, 2
= 11, 12
Disables the Softstart Mode, but does not remove 
previously loaded softstart values.
The softstart values defined by set_softstart_level are 
put out as analog voltage values at the ANALOG OUT1 
port.
The softstart values defined by set_softstart_level are 
put out as analog voltage values at the ANALOG OUT2 
port.
The change from one Level to the next occurs with the 
trailing edge of the laser pulse.
The change from one Level to the next occurs with the 
leading edge of the laser pulse.
number
1…1000
(number+1) is the number of softstart values to be 
transmitted.
restartdelay
0…65534
(1 bit equals 
10 µs)
Defines the time period for which the laser must have 
been switched off before softstart is activated at the 
next switch-on.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_softstart_mode (mode, number, restartdelay: word);
C:
void set_softstart_mode (unsigned short mode, unsigned short number, 
unsigned short restartdelay); 
Basic:
sub set_softstart_mode (ByVal mode%, ByVal number%, ByVal restartdelay%)
Comments
• set_softstart_mode must be called before first-time use of the set_softstart_level 
command.
• The individual softstart values level(0)…level(number) must be provided individually by 
separate calls of set_softstart_level. Indices for which no level value was supplied are 
undefined.
• When Softstart Mode is switched off, the already transmitted values are not deleted 
and can be further used after a renewed switch-on.
• The power of the first laser pulse is determined by level(1) if the values are assigned 
with the leading edge of the laser pulse selected, or by level(0) if the trailing edge of 
the laser pulse is selected.
• See also Chapter 4.6.4, “Softstart Mode”, Page 53. 
References

set_standby
Function
Defines the output period and the pulse length of the stand-by pulses or – in Laser Mode 4 
– the continuously-running laser signals.
Parameters
half_period
Half of the stand-by output period. In bits. 
1 bit equals 1/8 µs.
Allowed range: [0…65500].
pulse_width
Pulse length of the stand-by pulses. In bits. 
1 bit equals 1/8 µs.
Allowed range: [0…half_period].* 
• If a value larger than half_period is specified, the RTC4 driver sets the 
pulse_width to half_period.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_standby(half_period, pulse_width: word);
C:
void set_standby(unsigned short half_period, unsigned short pulse_width);
Basic:
sub set_standby(ByVal half_period%, ByVal pulse_width%)
Comments
• The clock frequency for the stand-by pulses is always 8 MHz. 
1 bit equals 1/8 µs.
• The stand-by pulses are available in all laser modes (YAG Mode 1, YAG Mode 2, YAG 
Mode 3, CO2 Mode, Laser Mode 4). They can be turned off by setting the stand-by 
pulse length to zero (default).
• The laser mode is set by set_laser_mode. 
See also Chapter 4.6, “Laser Control”, Page 48.
• To set the active output period and pulse length for the two laser signals, use the 
list command set_laser_timing.

[p.195]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
11 RTC4 Commands 
195
innovators for industry
Comments 
• The set_trigger call always causes exactly 32768 values per measurement channel to 
be measured and stored onto the RTC4. Afterward, get_waveform can be used to 
transfer the measured values to the PC for evaluation.
• The current status of a measurement session can be queried by measurement_status. 
• Once started, a measurement session can only be canceled by again calling set_trigger. 
Previously measured values are thereby lost.
• The type of scan system being used determines which status signals are generated and 
returned by the status channels. Specific information can be found in your scan system 
operating manual.
• For scan systems with only one status channel, the status signals are only readable if 
signal1,2 = 1 or signal1,2 = 4. 
• Coordinate Transformations defined by set_matrix, set_matrix_list, set_offset or 
set_offset_list are already reflected in the SampleX, SampleY and SampleZ Cartesian 
output values.
• The SampleAX_Corr…SampleBZ_Corr output values are the (digital) output values 
actually transmitted from the RTC4 to the scan system. The RTC4 computes these values 
while taking into account the SampleX, SampleY, SampleZ output values as well as the 
selected correction file. 
References
get_waveform, measurement_status, control_command, get_value

innovators for industry
List Command
set_wobbel
Function
Defines a circular motion of the output position which is added to the regular marking 
motion.
Parameters
amplitude
Amplitude of the circular wobbel motion. In bits. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed range: [1…5000].
frequency
Frequency of the wobbel motion in Hz 
(circles per second). 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Allowed range: [1…6000].
Integration
Pascal:
procedure set_wobbel(amplitude: word; frequency: double);
C:
void set_wobbel(unsigned short amplitude, double frequency);
Basic:
sub set_wobbel(ByVal amplitude%, ByVal frequency#)
Comments
• Calling the command set_wobbel sets the wobbel phase to a defined starting value 
(which is independent of the direction of the marking vector).
• Wobbel Mode can be used for marking lines with variable line width.
• A circular motion is added to the linear marking motion, resulting in a spiral motion of 
the laser focus in the Image Field.
• A broad line is obtained by choosing suitable values for the amplitude and the 
frequency. The amplitude and the frequency must be appropriate for the current 
marking speed.
• Wobbel Mode is terminated by setting the amplitude to zero.
• When defining the parameter (amplitude and frequency) take the dynamics of the 
scan head and laser into account. Otherwise, an overheating and even a permanent 
damage of the system may occur, see Chapter 5.2.1, “Wobbel Shapes – Important 
Notes on Choosing Appropriate Parameter Values”, Page 60.
References
set_mark_speed

innovators for industry
List Command
simulate_ext_start 
Function
Starts the next list automatically after a specified delay (counter pulses). 
Prerequisite 
Enabled Option Processing-on-the-fly. 
Parameters
delay 
See comments. 
As a signed 16-bit value. 
encoder 
= 0:
Use ENCODER X. 
= 1:
Use ENCODER Y. 
Integration
Pascal:
procedure simulate_ext_start(delay, encoder: smallint);
C:
void simulate_ext_start(short delay, short encoder);
Basic:
sub simulate_ext_start(ByVal delay%, ByVal encoder%)
Comments
• See also Chapter 5.11, “Processing-on-the-fly Functionality”, Page 79. 
• simulate_ext_start is a list command. It should be used as the first command in a list. 
• simulate_ext_start can be only used together with a real encoder (hardware encoder), 
not together with simulate_encoder. 
• A separate counter is used for the start delay. When simulate_ext_start is executed, the 
RTC sets the counter to zero. Afterwards, the pulses from the selected encoder are 
counted. When the counter reaches the value [delay × 16], the external /START is 
performed. (The next list is started only if no list is executing at the moment, that is, if 
the current list is already finished.) 
• The counter pulses are counted with sign, that is, depending on the direction of the 
motion. If the object moves in the reverse direction, delay should be negative as well. 
• To specify the start position of the next list, use set_extstartpos_list. 
• The following applies for RTC4 only with RTC4D2.HEX V2.433 / RTC4D3.HEX V3.433 and 
RTC4DLL.DLL V440: encoder = 10 (as encoder = 0) can be used to select ENCODER X 
and encoder = 11 (as encoder = 1) to select ENCODER Y, too. 
With encoder = 10 or 11 (in contrast to encoder = 0 or 1), the list start is only executed, 
if the external /START (or /START2) signal is active, that is, if this signal has been enabled 
with set_control_mode and activated by a HIGH to LOW level transition. In addition, 
with encoder = 10 or 11 (in contrast to encoder = 0 or 1), the simulated start is ignored, 
when the maximum number of external /STARTS (defined by set_max_counts) has 
been reached. 
References
set_ext_start_delay, set_ext_start_delay_list, select_list, set_control_mode

List Command
timed_jump_abs
Function
Jump to the specified position in the Image Field using the specified duration.
Parameters
xval, 
yval
Absolute coordinates of the vector end point. In bits. 
Each: As a signed 16-bit value. 
time
Duration of the complete jump vector. In µs. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
Allowed range: [10…655350].
Integration
Pascal:
procedure timed_jump_abs(xval, yval: smallint; time: double);
C:
void timed_jump_abs(short xval, short yval, double time);
Basic:
sub timed_jump_abs(ByVal xval%, ByVal yval%, ByVal time#)
Comments
• The parameter time is rounded down to a multiple of 10 µs (within the allowed range).
• A timed jump command is not executed with the normal jump speed. Instead, the 
speed (that is, the number of Microsteps) is adjusted so that the vector lasts exactly as 
long as specified. 
See also Chapter 5.8, “Timed Jump Commands, Timed Mark Commands”, Page 73.
• After a timed jump, a Jump Delay is inserted, just like after a normal jump. 
That means the total time for the jump is the specified time plus the Jump Delay.
• Subsequent jump_abs / jump_rel (not timed) are executed with the normal 
jump speed. See also set_jump_speed.
References
set_scanner_delays, timed_jump_rel

Parameters
x
[1, 2]
ANALOG OUT1 / ANALOG OUT2 ports on the RTC4 board. 
[3, 4, 5, 6]
ANALOG OUT ports on the I/O Extension Board for RTC3/RTC4 
(Accessory) (optional). 
value
Output value for the DA converter. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Allowed range: [0…1023].
If a value > 1023 is specified, the output value is set to 1023.
Integration

C:

Basic:
sub write_da_x(ByVal x%, ByVal value%)
Comments
• For the ANALOG OUT1 / ANALOG OUT2 ports, the commands write_da_1 / write_da_2 
can be used alternatively (without parameter x).
• Note that the output range of the ANALOG OUT1 port can be either 0 V…2.50 V or 
0 V…10 V, see Chapter 9.1.2, “Signals at the Laser Connector”, Page 96. In contrast, 
the output range of the ANALOG OUT2 port is always 0 V…10 V. See also the 
“Installation and Operation I/O Extension Board” manual.

Ctrl Command
z_out
Function
Sends a 16-bit value directly to the Z channel of the RTC4 
(CHAN3; see Figure 26).
Parameters
value
Z output value. 
As a signed 16-bit value.
Integration
Pascal:
procedure z_out(value: smallint);
C:
void z_out(short value);
Basic:
sub z_out(ByVal value%)
Comments
• The output value is sent directly to the Z channel of the RTC4.
• The Z output value must be in the range –32768…+32767. 
• Important: z_out should only be used in 2D user programs. 
In 3D user programs which use the DSP Program File for 3D user programs RTC4D3.HEX, 
the RTC4 overwrites the z output value every 10 µs. 
See also Chapter 5.10, “3D Functionality”, Page 75.

12 RTC4 PCIe Board Troubleshooting 
208
innovators for industry
12 RTC4 PCIe Board Troubleshooting
If the problems persist, contact SCANLAB.
Problem 
Remedy 
PC does not boot 
Switch off the PC and check the following:
• Check if the RTC4 board is correctly seated in the PCI slot. 
Refer to the instructions in your PC manual.
• Check for metal parts that may have fallen into the PC housing during 
installation of the RTC4.
• Check for loose cables or connectors
RTC4 does not respond 
• Check the driver installation. 
See Chapter 10.1, “Installing the Software”, Page 101.
• Was the driver mistakenly installed after the RTC4 board was installed 
(driver installation should precede board installation)?
• Check the DLL import declarations in your user program. 
See Chapter 10.2, “DLL Calling Convention”, Page 103.
User program or OS fails 
• Check the driver installation and the driver version. 
See Chapter 2.6.2, “Software”, Page 19 and Chapter 10.1, “Installing 
the Software”, Page 101.
• Check the RTC4 initialization in the user program.
• Check the DLL import declarations in your user program. 
See Chapter 10.2, “DLL Calling Convention”, Page 103.
Scan head control fails 
• Check if the scan head is properly connected to the RTC4 by the data 
cable. Make sure to follow the specifications for the data cable. 
See Chapter 6.5, “Data Cable”, Page 88.
• Check the power supply of the scan head. Refer to your scan head 
manual.
• Check your user program.
Laser control fails 
• Check the interface between the RTC4 and the laser.
Irregular marking results 
• Check the laser and Scanner Delays. 
See Chapter 4.3.3, “Notes on Optimizing the Delays”, Page 40.
Laser does not switch off during 
jump[*] Commands 
• Check the laser and Scanner Delays. 
See Section “Explanations”, Page 41.

13 Customer Service
13.1 Servicing and Repairs
All servicing and repairs should be performed only at 
SCANLAB.The warranty expires if the board has been 
altered.
13.2 Warranty
SCANLAB guarantees this product to be free of 
defects in manufacturing and material. The warranty 
is valid for 12 months after delivery. Repairs covered 
under the warranty are performed at SCANLAB.
The scope of the warranty is limited to repair or 
replacement of the SCANLAB product.
SCANLAB is responsible for the return delivery of 
products repaired under warranty; the customer is 
responsible for delivery to SCANLAB.
SCANLAB is not held responsible:
• when the product has been damaged through 
misuse or improper operation
• for repairs not performed by SCANLAB
• if the RTC4 board has been altered
• for damage resulting from improper packaging of 
a product returned to SCANLAB
• for consequential damages
13.3 Contacting SCANLAB
For service, repairs, advice or information, simply 
contact SCANLAB using one of the contact 
possibilities listed below:
SCANLAB GmbH
Siemensstr. 2a
82178 Puchheim
Germany

Fax: +49 (89) 800 746-199
info@scanlab.de
www.scanlab.de

The RTC4 can be returned to SCANLAB for a fee to be 
properly disposed of.

14 Legal

innovators for industry
14.2 Compliance with FCC Rules 
– RTC4 PCIe Board
The RTC4 PCIe Board has been tested and found to 
comply with the limits for a Class A digital device, 
pursuant to part 15 of the FCC rules.
These limits are designed to provide reasonable 
protection against harmful interference when the 
RTC4 PCIe Board is operated in a commercial 
environment. The RTC4 PCIe Board generates, uses, 
and can radiate radio frequency energy and, if not 
installed and used in accordance with this instruction 
manual, may cause harmful interference to radio 
communications. Operation of the RTC4 PCIe Board 
in a residential area is likely to cause harmful 
interference in which case the user is required to 
correct the interference at his own expense.

16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
214
innovators for industry
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board
16.1 Product Overview
16.1.1 RTC4 Ethernet Board vs. 
RTC4 PCIe Board – Usage and 
Comparison
RTC4 Ethernet Board and RTC4 PCIe Board share the 
same core functionality: 
• Real-time control of the laser and scan system.
• Transfer of direct commands from the PC to the 
RTC4. The commands are executed immediately.
• Transfer of list commands from the PC to RTC4 list 
memory. These commands execute only after the 
list is started.
• List processing occurs in real time.
• Calculation of the set position occurs every 10 µs. 
• Image Field correction is applied to the 
set position.
• The interface to the scan system uses the 16-bit 
XY2-100 protocol (not the 20-bit SL2-100 
protocol). 
The RTC4 Ethernet Board differs from 
RTC4 PCIe Board in the following respects: 
• Ethernet interface instead of PCIe bus, that is: 
– Communication with the PC is by TCP/IP and 
UDP instead of PCIe.
– No RTC4 driver installation 
(instead, RTC4netDll.dll or RTC4netDllx64.dll 
is used, see below). 
– Rather than in a PC, it can be installed, for 
example, in an electric control cabinet. A 
dedicated PC near the laser system is 
unnecessary. 
• Only the RTC4 Ethernet Board has an 
RS-232 interface for controlling an external 
device (via RS-232 socket connector and 
corresponding commands, see page 226). 
• The following is possible with RTC4 Ethernet 
Boards (but not required): 
– The 1. SCANHEAD socket connector can be 
used to power the first scan head. 
– The 2. SCANHEAD socket connector, if factory-
enabled by SCANLAB, can be used to power a 
second scan head.
• For software development, the following is 
supplied: 
– RTC4ethDLL.dll 
(for 32-bit user programs, to be used instead of 
RTC4DLL.dll(1)) 
– RTC4ethDLLx64.dll 
(for 64-bit user programs, 
to be used instead of RTC4DLLx64.dll(1)) 
– RTC4netDll.dll 
(for 32-bit user programs(1)) 
– RTC4netDllx64.dll 
(for 64-bit user programs(1)) 
– Import declaration files for various 
development platforms 
• RTC4 I/O boards cannot be used with the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
• The RTC4 Ethernet Board does not support: 
– RTC4-Circular Queue Mode 
– Stepper motor control (for varioSCAN FLEX)
(1) Needs to be in the same directory of the executable 
file.

[p.215]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
215
innovators for industry
In contrast to RTC SCANalone boards
• The RTC4 Ethernet Board offers no 
RTC SCANalone functionality. It cannot operate 
as a “stand-alone” controller, that is, without a 
PC. 
• The RTC4 Ethernet Board list memory size is 
limited. Unlike the RTC SCANalone, its memory 
cannot be expanded by an MMC card. 
• With its Ethernet connection, the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board achieves significantly higher data transfer 
rates between it and the PC (in both directions), 
as compared to an RTC SCANalone with USB 1.1.
• You can operate an RTC4 Ethernet Board near 
your laser system (the “Machine”), whereas the 
RTC SCANalone operates near the PC. 
• The RTC4 Ethernet Board is not designed for the 
following key RTC SCANalone usage scenario 
(which requires a dedicated PC per “Machine”): 
– Copying the user program onto an MMC at the 
PC. 
– Successively inserting the MMC into multiple 
RTC SCANalone boards for the purpose of 
copying the user program onto each individual 
board. 
– Then have these boards autonomously process 
jobs. 
Caution!
• To avoid interference coupling and emissions, 
never operate the RTC4 Ethernet Board without 
shielding (for example, outside a metal 
housing). 
• The RTC4 Ethernet Board is designed exclusively 
for industrial use. It is intended for integration 
in a machine (typically in a laser system) and 
does not fulfill all requirements of a ready-to-
use consumer end product. Only operate the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board after integration in a 
machine meeting all applicable directives and 
standards (of your local jurisdiction). It is not 
suitable for use as a toy, in households or 
inclement environments (for example, 
outdoors). The operator must take appropriate 
precautionary measures to prevent such 
improper usage. 
• Installation and commissioning should only be 
performed by personnel with sufficient 
qualifications, for example, knowledge of 
electrical equipment safety. Only perform 
installation and maintenance if power and 
lasers are switched off. 
• Because the RTC4 Ethernet Board is a Class A 
device capable of generating interference in 
residential areas, the operator may be required 
to carry out appropriate measures.

[p.216]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US

innovators for industry
16.1.2 System Requirements
Hardware
• Shielded housing (for example, electric control 
cabinet) with:
– Provisions for mechanical mounting, incl. 
mounting hardware
– Power outlet
– Ethernet cable 
– Power supply as specified
– Cable with connector for powering the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board
– Flat ribbon cables for peripheral equipment 
(laser, scan head, extensions)
• Windows PC (a dedicated PC next to the Machine 
is not required)
• 10/100 Mbit/s Ethernet
Software
• TCP/IP protocol IPv4
• UDP protocol
• The ports for TCP and UDP (see Required local 
ports, Page 271) must not be blocked. 
For the development of user programs: 
• DLL/Import declarations
– RTC4ethDLL.dll/RTC4ethDLLx64.dll 
(instead of RTC4DLL.dll/RTC4DLLx64.dll)
– RTC4netDll.dll/RTC4netDllx64.dll 
(instead of the RTC4 Board driver)
Important: Both files, RTC4ethDLL.dll and 
RTC4netDll.dll (RTC4ethDLLx64.dll and 
RTC4netDllx64.dll, respectively), must come from the 
same release date! Other combinations are not 
allowed and result in faulty user programs.
 
Notes on allowed combinations can be found in the 
file changelog.txt (part of the delivered software 
package), sections “Release Date…”. 
Example: In section “Release Date 2015-12-18” are 
mentioned RTC4netDll.dll V.1.7 and RTC4ethDLL.dll 
version 4.63 and therefore, must be used together.

RTC4 Ethernet Board. In contrast to the 
RTC4 PCIe Board software package are included: 
– Specific dynamic link libraries 
(RTC4ethDLL.dll, RTC4ethDLLx64.dll,

import declaration files
– Files with sample source code 
16.1.7 Options

Page 93. 
16.1.8 Supplementary Software
To facilitate customizing correction files basing on 
your own test measurements, SCANLAB offers its 
correXion line of software and related 
documentation. See also Chapter 4.5.2, “Image Field 
Correction Algorithm”, Page 47.

ETHERNET Connector
• Position on the board: front side, see Figure 34, 
number 8.
• Purpose: to connect to the network.
• For status indication the following LEDs are part 
of the connector:
– LED yellow, function “IP Assignment OK”. 
The LED is permanently on as soon as the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board has an assigned 
IP address (static IP, DHCP, or auto-IP). 
Note: Without programmed static IP address 
the switched-on LED indicates that the 
IP address assignment has been carried-out 
successfully by DHCP or auto IP. In case if there 
is a programmed static IP address a switched-
on LED does not mean that the IP address is 
valid in the subnet in every case. 
– LED green, function “Link / Traffic”. 
The LED is permanently on as soon as a 
connection is established (“Link”). This is 
usually the case when the Ethernet cable is 
plugged-in and there is an active router or LAN 
adapter at the remote end. 
The LED flashes when there is network traffic 
(“Traffic”).

BUSY Status LED
• Position on the board: front side, see Figure 34,
number 13. 
• The BUSY Status LED is a red LED which is 
electrically coupled with the BUSY status signal(1). 
Therefore, it is only on during a list execution. 
• Furthermore, the moment the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board is powered, the BUSY Status LED goes on 
briefly and immediately off again.

• Position on the board (only boards as of delivery 
date 2018-09): front side, see Figure 34, number 
14.

RS-232 interface. 
• Pin-out:

– Max. output voltage range:

– The signals are referenced to GND(2).

1× PicoBlade Housing

Part No. 50079-8100 (or 50058-8000). 
• By rs232_config, baud rate, number of stop bits 
and the parity can be set. The number of data bits 
(frame length) cannot be changed. 
• About signal output via RS-232 Interface: 
The RS-232 socket connector (see Figure 41) 
provides an RS-232 interface. The interface can be 
configured by rs232_config. rs232_write_data 
can be used to send single data bytes to the 
RS-232 interface. Character strings (strings) can 
be sent via the interface by rs232_write_text. 
• About signal input via RS-232 Interface: 
The RS-232 socket connector (see Figure 41) 
provides an RS-232 interface for reading signals. 
The interface can be configured by rs232_config. 
Data can be read by rs232_read_data.

16.2.3 Interface to the PC
Unlike RTC4 PCIe Boards, the RTC4 Ethernet Board 
does not have a PCIe-x1-connector. Instead, it has an 
RJ-45 connector (more specific: RJ connector of type 
8P8C) for the Ethernet connection, see Section 
“ETHERNET Connector”, Page 223.

[p.228]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
228
innovators for industry
16.3 Installation and Operation 
16.3.1 Possible Approaches to 
Powering Scan Heads
In principle, the RTC4 Ethernet Board offers the 
following approaches for supplying power to a 
scan head, see Figure 42 and Figure 43: 
• Approach 1 
– A separate supply exists to power the 
scan head. 
– The RTC4 Ethernet Board gets its own power 
supply. 
– Recommended for scan heads with high power 
consumption such as the intelliWELD system.
• Approach 2 
– A shared supply powers both the scan head 
and the RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
– This arrangement is suited, for example, for 
scan heads with 25-pin Sub-D connectors for 
data and power, such as the hurrySCAN and 
SCANcube.
16.3.2 Hardware Installation
Proceed as follows to install the RTC4 Ethernet Board 
in a shielded housing: 
4 Remove the RTC4 Ethernet Board from its anti-
static bag. Do not touch the electrical contacts of 
the board.
4 Mount the RTC4 Ethernet Board at the intended 
location in your shielded housing. 
4 Connect the RTC4 Ethernet Board to: 
– your power supply using a power cable
– your Ethernet port using an Ethernet cable
4 Connect the RTC4 Ethernet Board using 
appropriate cables to: 
– the scan head (see also page 88, observe the 
information about the ferrit)
– the laser
– any handling system or other peripherals of the 
overall machine.
4 If want to use the signals at the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board socket connectors, then attach appropriate 
cables. 
Caution!
• Store the RTC4 Ethernet Board in an 
electrostatically neutral environment using the 
supplied anti-static bag.
• Observe ESD precautions when installing the 
board.
• Do not touch the electrical contacts of the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board.
• Protect the board from moisture, dust, corrosive 
vapors and mechanical loads.
