16.3.3 Software Installation
Unlike RTC4 PCIe Boards, the RTC4 Ethernet Board 
requires no drivers or setup programs. 
Instead of installing a driver, you must copy the 
following supplied software package files to an 
appropriate directory on the network PC(1) (simplest: 
as with the RTC4ethDLL.dll/RTC4ethDLLx64.dll file, 
into the user program working directory): 
• RTC4netDll.dll/RTC4netDllx64.dll 
To develop user programs, you must copy the 
following supplied software package file to an 
appropriate directory (1) on the network PC:
• RTC4ethDLL.dll (for 32-bit user programs) or 
RTC4ethDLLx64.dll (for 64-bit user programs) 
Remark: The RTC4DLL.dll and RTC4DLLx64.dll are 
only usable with RTC4 PCIe Boards. They cannot 
be used with RTC4 Ethernet Boards. 
And you can copy the import declaration files to your 
software project directory (or directories).
16.3.4 Initial Startup (Test, Without 
User Programs)
Prerequisite: The RTC4 Ethernet Board is installed (as 
described above) and Ethernet is available.
After the board receives power(2) and connects to the 
network, an IP address gets assigned(3). 
During that process the LEDs at the ETHERNET
connector indicate the status, see Section “ETHERNET 
Connector”, Page 223. Depending on your 
infrastructure, the IP address is assigned by a DHCP 
server (takes around 15 s) or the auto-IP / link-local 
address method (takes up to 45 s). 
After receiving the IP address successfully the yellow 
LED of the ETHERNET connector is permanently on, 
see also Section “ETHERNET Connector”, Page 223. 
Do a visual check for verification. 
To identify the current IP address of your 
RTC4 Ethernet Board you have the following 
possibilities: 
• to use the delivered 
RTC4eth Configuration Tool, see also the 
separate document RTC4eth Configuration 
Tool.pdf. Among other things the tool allows you 
to find and identify RTC4 Ethernet Boards in a 
network, readout their properties (such as 
MAC address and IP address), and to store a 
static IP address.
• the user interface of your router
• software coded by yourself. For that purpose you 
can make use of the delivered source code for 
demo programs.
(1) In the Internet, search, for example, for the term 
“Dynamic Link Library Search Order” 
(2) The BUSY status LED single-flashes and after that it is 
off.
(3) At initial installation the board does not have a static 
IP address.

[p.232]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
232
innovators for industry
16.4 Notes on Migrating Existing 
and Programming New RTC4 
User Programs
Application source code is very similar for both 
RTC4 Ethernet Boards and RTC4 PCIe Boards. The 
differences are: 
• A different dynamic link library is bound: 
– RTC4ethDLL.dll 
for 32-bit user programs 
– RTC4ethDLLx64.dll 
for 64-bit user programs 
• Other import declarations must be included. 
• As of RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.81, exclusive access to a 
specific RTC4 Ethernet Board (just like with 
RTC4 PCIe Boards) is by board number. However, 
it must have been assigned before by assign_rtc 
or assign_rtc_by_ip. 
As a consequence, source code written for 
RTC4 PCIe Boards need to be updated 
correspondingly (see following 3 sections and 
example code on page 235). 
Case a): known IP address and 1 or more 
RTC4 Ethernet Board(s) in network 
By assign_rtc_by_ip, a card number must be 
assigned to the board first. Since the IP address is 
known, no call of rtc_search_cards is necessary 
before. You can also proceed as if the IP address is 
unknown (see below). 
Before calling other card-specific commands, the 
next call must be acquire_rtc(1) which establishes an 
exclusive connection. The legacy source code can 
then follow unchanged. At the end of the program, 
boards previously acquired by acquire_rtc must be 
correctly released again by release_rtc. 
Case b): unknown IP address and only 1 
RTC4 Ethernet Board in network 
Whether one or more RTC4 Ethernet Boards are in the 
network is irrelevant with regard to their control from 
RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.81 on. 
Case c): unknown IP address and several 
RTC4 Ethernet Boards in network 
First the cards are searched for in the network by 
rtc_search_cards. By assign_rtc, a user-defined 
board number is then assigned to each board from 
the found boards via its search number. The board 
can then be identified for example, by 
get_mac_address or get_serial. The assigned 
number can be removed by remove_rtc. 
By acquire_rtc, the corresponding board with the 
given board number is then acquired, that is, an 
exclusive connection is established(1)(2). Afterwards 
the previous source code follows. At the end of the 
program, previously acquired boards must be 
released again by release_rtc. 
Remark: as of RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.81, acquire_rtc and 
release_rtc work with the board number and no 
longer with the IP address. 
For a reliable and safe operation it is mandatory to 
check the current network status at relevant source 
code lines and the correct transmission of the 
commands from and to the RTC4 Ethernet Board, see 
eth_get_last_error. 
Notes 
• The recommended order of the commands 
load_program_file and load_correction_file as 
described in Chapter 10.3, “Initializing the 
RTC4 PCIe Board”, Page 105 does also apply to 
RTC4 Ethernet Boards.
(1) Once the exclusive connection has been established 
successfully a static IP address could be assigned by 
set_static_ip at this point of time.
(2) The exclusive connection is established via TCP, see 
Required local ports, Page 271. This connection is used 
to transfer control commands and list commands.

[p.233]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
233
innovators for industry
16.4.1 Compatibility Mode
RTC4ethDLL.dll/RTC4ethDLLx64.dll V4.81 
(RTC4eth V2 Software Release 2020-05-15) offer a 
“Compatibility Mode” with which the behavior of 
V4.79 can be set: 
• Only a single RTC4 Ethernet Board is supported 
(no multi-board support, see also Section ”Note 
on Multi-Board Support”, Page 237) 
• For multi-board commands (n_) “1” is the only 
valid board number 
• Not allowed: 
– assign_rtc 
– assign_rtc_by_ip 
– remove_rtc 
– select_rtc 
Compatibility Mode is automatically activated by the 
first acquire_rtc( card_no ) call, if the card_no value 
(instead of a board number from the DLL-internal 
RTC4 board management) is an IPv4 address (as 
unsigned 32 bit value, see convert_string_to_ip). 
Notes
• The following applies for acquire_rtc(0): 
– The parameter 0 is interpreted as IPv4 address 
– Triggers a network search 
– Acquires the first RTC4 Ethernet Board found in 
Compatibility Mode 
– A subsequent release_rtc call with any 
IPv4 address (Bit 31…Bit 24 0) releases the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board which has been previously 
acquired by acquire_rtc(0).

[p.234]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
234
innovators for industry
16.4.2 Finding RTC4 Ethernet Boards 
in the Network and Querying 
their Properties
• All RTC4 Ethernet Boards in a network can be 
searched with rtc_search_cards and counted. 
This always occurs before assign_rtc and the 
following acquire_rtc. 
• Each found RTC4 Ethernet Board can be queried, 
for example: 
– IP address with get_ip_address 
(see also convert_ip_to_string)
– MAC address with get_mac_address 
(see also convert_mac_to_string)
– Serial number with get_serial 
– IP address of the master with 
get_master_ip_address
– Connection status with
get_connection_status 
Assigning a Static IP Address 
In industry, static IP addresses are often assigned to 
network devices. By set_static_ip, you can assign a 
static IP address to an RTC4 Ethernet Board 
(jumper X12 can be in any position, see page 226). 
The static IP address is stored in the nonvolatile 
memory of the board. It is used if jumper X12 is not 
in “force DHCP position” when the board is switched 
on. 
SCANLAB recommends to use static IP addresses at 
least with production systems.
Forcing IP Address Assignment by DHCP or 
auto-IP Despite Static IP Address 
It may happen that the stored IP address 
configuration does not (no longer) match the 
network used. Using the jumper X12, see “X12 
Jumper Field”, Page 226, you can force the IP address 
assignment by DHCP or auto-IP: 
(1) Switch-off the power supply of the board. 
(2) Put Jumper X12 in “force DHCP position”, see 
“X12 Jumper Field”, Page 226.
(3) Switch-on the power supply of the board. 
The saved static IP address is not used now. The 
board receives its IP address by the DHCP server 
or auto-IP, see Chapter 16.3.4, “Initial Startup 
(Test, Without User Programs)”, Page 231. 
(4) Depending on the method of IP address 
assignment wait approx. 40 seconds (auto-IP) or 
approx 15 seconds (DHCP).

[p.235]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board

innovators for industry
16.4.3 Example Code (C++) – 
Initializing a User Program 
with Several RTC4 Ethernet 
Boards
//
Abstract
//
A console application to demonstrate how to search RTC4 Ethernet boards and 
//
show corresponding information.
//
//
Comment
//
This application demonstrates how to properly search for RTC4 Ethernet boards
//
in a given IP subnet. It will enumerate all available RTC4 Ethernet boards, 
//
show their IP addresses and serial numbers.
//
Prerequisite for the RTC4 Ethernet boards: RTC4eth_FW_2.0.6.0.bin or higher must be installed. 
//
//
Platform
//
Win32 - 32-bit Windows 
//
//
Necessary Files
//
RTC4ethimpl.h
//
RTC4ethDLL.dll and RTC4netDll.dll for Win32
//
RTC4ethDLL.lib for Win32
//
//
Compiler
//
- tested with Microsoft C/C++ Optimization Compiler 19.00.24210.
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>
#include <stdio.h>
#include "RTC4ethimpl.h"
#pragma comment(lib, "RTC4ethDLL.lib")
// RTC4ethDLL.dll automatically initializes RTC4netDll.dll!
int main(int argc, char *argv[])
{
uint16_t num_found_cards;
uint32_t res, card_ip;
char ipbuff[16];
rtc_search_cards(&num_found_cards,
convert_string_to_ip("192.168.250.1"),
convert_string_to_ip("255.255.255.0"));
if (num_found_cards == 0) {
printf("Error, no RTC4 Ethernet boards found.\n");
return EXIT_FAILURE;
}

[p.236]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
236
innovators for industry
for (int i = 1; i <= num_found_cards; i++) {
// assign card #i the user number i (1:1 mapping)
if (assign_rtc(i, i) != i) {
printf("Error, could not assign id %d to board #%d.\n", i, i);
return EXIT_FAILURE;
}
// select card #i with an intrinsic acquire
select_rtc(i);
card_ip = get_ip_address(i);
convert_ip_to_string(card_ip, ipbuff);
printf("Board #%d has IP: %s and serial %d.\n", i, ipbuff, n_get_serial_number_32(i)); 
} 
for (int i = num_found_cards; i > 0; i--) { 
release_rtc(i); 
} 
return EXIT_SUCCESS;
}

16.5 RTC4 Commands – Not Usable

The following commands cannot be used with 
V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards:
• move_to 
• rtc4_count_cards 
16.6 RTC4 Ethernet 
BoardCommands and

Note on Multi-Board Support
As of RTC4eth V2 Software Release 2020-05-15, is 
possible to simultaneously use several RTC4 Ethernet 
Boards available within a network by one 
user program like it is possible with other 
RTC4 boards. 
That is, there is even multi-board support for 
RTC4 Ethernet Boards because 
RTC4ethDLL.dll/RTC4ethDLLx64.dll now contain 
multi-board commands (n_). 
See also Chapter 16.4.1, “Compatibility Mode”, 
Page 233.

Ctrl Command
assign_rtc
Function
Assigns a user-defined board number to a RTC4 Ethernet Board found by 
rtc_search_cards. 
Call
assign_rtc( search_no, card_no )
Result
Error code. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
Board number 
In case of success. 
0
In case of error. 
Parameters
search_no 1…number of found RTC4 Ethernet Boards (= returned parameter value 
&cards of rtc_search_cards). 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
card_no 
Desired user-defined board number. 
Allowed value range: [0…65,535]. 
As an unsigned 16-bit value. 
Comments
• By the user-defined card number, all further RTC4 Ethernet Board accesses are carried 
out by either 
– the multi-board commands (n_) or 
– the RTC4 Ethernet Board that has been globally set by select_rtc 
• For card_no = 0, in case of success the next free RTC4 Ethernet Board number is used 
and returned. 
• assign_rtc is not available as a multi-board command (n_). 
• The complementary command of assign_rtc (and assign_rtc_by_ip) is remove_rtc. 
• See also Chapter 16.4.1, “Compatibility Mode”, Page 233. 
References
rtc_search_cards, assign_rtc_by_ip, remove_rtc, select_rtc

Like assign_rtc. 
Parameters

IP address in Little Endian format. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
card_no 
Like assign_rtc.

Ctrl Command
eth_get_error
Function
Returns an accumulated error code. It contains all errors which occurred with the most 
recently executed RTC4 Ethernet Board commands. 
Call
EthAccError = eth_get_error()
Parameters
None. 
Result 
Error code. Identical to eth_get_last_error. See Section “Error Codes with 
V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards”, Page 265. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
If multiple errors occurred simultaneously, then multiple bits are set. 
Comments
• eth_get_error and n_eth_get_error are available even without explicit access rights 
to a specific RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
• If with an RTC4 Ethernet Board command call (internally) several errors occur 
successively, eth_get_last_error probably returns only the very last error (for example, 
only “not_acquired”). The actual error causes can be identified by eth_get_error 
because it returns the accumulated errors.
• The accumulated error is reset automatically with each acquiring of the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board. 
• eth_get_error is provided for consistency with the RTC6 command set. 
Version info
Available as of RTC4netDll.dll V2.4.0.0 and RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.86. 
References
acquire_rtc, eth_get_last_error

Ctrl Command
eth_get_last_error 
Function
Returns an error status which refers to the Ethernet connection only. 
Replaces eth_status (deprecated). 
Call
eth_get_last_error( ) 
Parameters
None. 
Result
Error code. Identical to eth_get_error. See Section “Error Codes with V2 RTC4 Ethernet 
Boards”, Page 265. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value.
Parameters
None. 
Comments
• Only some commands for the RTC4 Ethernet Board, see also the list at the beginning of 
Chapter 16.6.2, “Command Set for the RTC4 Ethernet Board”, Page 238, return a 
detailed connection related error cause. 
• The “conventional” (that is, RTC4 commands which are not exclusively for the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board) RTC4 commands load_varpolydelay, load_program_file, 
load_correction_file, load_z_table and teachin have been extended (as of version 
2015-08) with the additional error code 14 (0xE), which indicates an Ethernet 
connection fault. For these commands and all other “conventional” RTC4 commands 
that do not return an error code, the specific Ethernet error code can be queried using 
eth_get_last_error. 
• After every critical RTC4 command or command sequence, a call to eth_get_last_error 
it is strongly recommended in order to verify whether a transmission to the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board has been successful, see also Section “Error Codes with 
V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards”, Page 265.

innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
eth_set_com_timeouts_auto
Function
Enables and sets the adaptive network communication timeout adjustment 
(“adaptive mode”). 
Call
eth_set_com_timeouts_auto( initial_timeout_ms, sum_timeout_ms, multiplicator,
mode )
Result
None. 
Parameters
initial_timeout_ms 
Start value of the network communication timeout. In ms. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
sum_timeout_ms 
Limit value of the total network communication timeout (including 
repetitions) for each executed RTC4 command. In ms. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
multiplicator 
Multiplication factor for network communication timeout 
adjustment. 
As a 64-bit IEEE floating point value. 
mode 
Reserved. Should be set to 1. Currently ignored. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
Returned 
parameter 
values
None. 
Comments 
• An eth_set_com_timeouts_auto call switches the behavior of network 
communication timeouts to “adaptive mode”. “Adaptive mode” is active by default 
with RTC4eth V2 Software Release 2020-10-16. In “adaptive mode”, communication 
is repeated when initial_timeout_ms is exceeded until the total time of all repetitions 
is greater than the limit value sum_timeout_ms. Meanwhile, the effective value of 
initial_timeout_ms is multiplied by multiplicator for each repetition. Each 
communication attempt starts with the original value of initial_timeout_ms. The 
default values are: 
– initial_timeout_ms = 1 
– sum_timeout_ms = 20 
– multiplicator = 1.2 
• An eth_set_com_timeouts_auto call switches from the default behavior (of the 
RTC4ethDLL.dll) with network communication timeouts to “adaptive mode”. In 
”adaptive mode”, the initially valid maximum allowed duration is increased by 
multiplication by multiplicator for each timeout. The network communication is then 
repeated until the total time of all repetitions is greater than the limit value 
sum_timeout_ms. 
• When using eth_set_com_timeouts_auto, the parameter values for the “adaptive 
mode” have to be set individually for each RTC4 Ethernet Board if changes are required. 
• set_timeouts (deprecated) deactivates the “adaptive mode” for the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board previously selected by select_rtc. eth_set_com_timeouts_auto has to be called 
explicitly for each individual RTC4 Ethernet Board to switch the “adaptive mode” back 
on.

[p.250]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
250
innovators for industry
Comments 
(cont’d) 
• The submitted parameter values are checked for plausibility and corrected (if 
necessary): 
– Negative signs are removed 
– The multiplicator value is adjusted so that the sequence of the allowed time 
intervals increases strictly monotonously 
Version info

Ctrl Command
eth_watchdog_timer_config
Function
Enables (disables) the “watchdog” functionality. 
Sets the “watchdog” timer start value on the RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
Call
actual_timer_ms = eth_watchdog_timer_config( timer_ms )
Result
Actually set “watchdog” timer start value on the RTC4 Ethernet Board (that is, after any 
clipping and/or rounding, see below).
0, if the “watchdog” functionality is switched off. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
Parameters 
timer_ms 
0: 
The “watchdog” functionality is disabled. 
Default after a Hardware Reset. 
[100…10,000]: The “watchdog” functionality is enabled. 
Start value of the “watchdog” timer. In ms. 
Out-of-range values are clipped to the 
boundary values. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
Comments
• As of the eth_watchdog_timer_config call: 
– The RTC4 Ethernet Board internally counts down the “watchdog” timer 
– As soon as it reaches 0: 
• stop_execution is executed 
• The “watchdog” timer is reset to timer_ms 
• The “watchdog” functionality remains enabled 
• The “watchdog” timer can be reset manually to timer_ms by 
eth_watchdog_timer_reset. 
• The “watchdog” timer value is rounded to an integer multiple of 10 ms. 
• load_program_file does not disable the “watchdog” functionality and does not 
change the “watchdog” timer start value. 
• See also Chapter 16.6.4, “Checking the Connection to the RTC4 Ethernet Board”, 
Page 266. 
Version info 
Available as of RTC4netDll.dll V2.3.0.0, RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.84 and MCU Firmware 
V2.0.7.0. 
References
eth_watchdog_timer_reset

innovators for industry
Ctrl Command
rs232_read_data
Function
Reads out a value from the ring buffer (for incoming values from the RS-232 interface. 
Call
rs232_read_data( &RS232Data )
Result
Error code. See Section “Error Codes with V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards”, Page 265. 
As unsigned 32-bit value. 
Returned 
parameter 
values 
RS232Data 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
Bit #0 (LSB) 
… 
Bit #7 
Read out value at the current read position in the ring buffer. 
If further characters are present in the ring buffer, the read 
position in the ring buffer is increased by one. 
Bit #8 
“New” bit. 
= 0:The value is outdated. That is, it has already been read out 
by rs232_read_data. 
= 1: The value is new. That is, it is read out for the first time 
with this read access. 
Bit #9 
… 
Bit #15 
0. 
Bit #16 
… 
Bit #23 
Number of further characters, which have not been read out 
yet. 
Bit #24 
“Overflow” bit: at least one character has been overwritten in 
the ring buffer. 
= 0: No values have been overwritten. 
= 1:At least 1 value has been overwritten. 
Bit #25 
… 
Bit #31 
Unused. 
Comments 
• Characters received from the RS-232 interface (see also page 226) are stored in a ring 
buffer (size: 256 characters). 
By rs232_read_data, they can be transferred to the user program (asynchronously to 
receipt) from there. 
• Byte #0 (Bit #0…Bit #7) contains the character from the current ring buffer reading 
position. 
• Byte #1 (Bit #8) indicates whether the character has already been read by the 
user program or not. 
• Byte #2 (Bit #16…Bit #23) indicates the number of characters in the ring buffer that 
still have not been read by the user program. If no unread characters are present 
(byte #2 = 0), then the most recently read character is transferred with “new bit” = 0.
• Byte #3 (Bit #24) (bit #24): indicates an overflow of the ring buffer. Normally it is 0. If 
one or more characters in the ring buffer have been overwritten, this is indicated by the 
value 1. The “Overflow” bit is reset by the readout.

[p.260]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
260
innovators for industry
Comments 
(cont’d) 
• Example: return value 459098 = 0x0007015A = (0, 7, 1, 90) means: character 90 ('Z') 
was read and is new (1), 7 additional characters remain to be read, no (due to ring 
buffer overrun) lost characters (0). 
References
rs232_write_data, rs232_write_text, rs232_config

Ctrl Command
set_static_ip
Function
Saves an static IP address, netmask and if required, a gateway address to the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board permanently. 
Call
set_static_ip( ip, netmask, gateway )
Result
Error code. See Section “Error Codes with V2 RTC4 Ethernet Boards”, Page 265. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value.
Parameters
ip 
User-defined static IP address. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value.
netmask 
User-defined static netmask. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value. 
gateway 
User-defined gateway address. 
As an unsigned 32-bit value.
Comments
• IP addresses “192.0.2.0/24” must not be used, see Chapter 16.6.3, “Note on Working 
with IP Addresses”, Page 266. 
• Jumper X12 can be in any position, see page 226 when programming the settings by 
set_static_ip. Upon next switch-on of the RTC4 Ethernet Board these settings are used 
for IP address assignment, provided that jumper X12 is not in “force DHCP position”. 
• The static IP address, netmask and if so, gateway address are stored permanently in the 
non-volatile memory of the RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
• If for any reason these settings shall not be used: see Section “Forcing IP Address 
Assignment by DHCP or auto-IP Despite Static IP Address”, Page 234.
• If permanently shall be switched back to DHCP/auto-IP address assignment a 
programmed static IP address can be erased by saving a zero (0, “0.0.0.0”).
• If the RTC4 Ethernet Board is in the same subnet as the NIC (supposed for 
communication), then the value 0 has to be specified instead of a gateway address. If 
the RTC4 Ethernet Board is in a different subnet as the NIC (supposed for 
communication) – in this case both are usually interconnected by a static route – then 
the corresponding gateway address has to be specified. 
• set_static_ip is not available as a multi-board command (n_). 
Version info
Last change with RTC4netDll.dll V.1.7 and RTC4ethDLL.dll V4.63: 
new parameter gateway.

16.6.3 Note on Working with IP 
Addresses
• IP addresses are stored in Big Endian Byte order. 
This means the most significant byte is stored 
first, that is, at the lowest memory address. 
• The commonly used dotted decimal notation (for 
example, 192.168.178.1) can be converted into 
its unsigned 32-bit integer equivalent as follows: 
uint32_t ip = 192 + (168 << 8) + (178 << 16) + 
(1 << 24) 
Alternatively, you can use the command 
convert_string_to_ip: 
uint32_t ip = 
convert_string_to_ip("192.168.178.1") 
• IP addresses “192.0.2.0/24” are reserved for 
internal test purposes and must not be used. 
See also RFC 5737 of the Internet Task Force. 
16.6.4 Checking the Connection to 
the RTC4 Ethernet Board
Communication via Ethernet is generally more 
unreliable than a PCIe bus connection inside a PC 
(simple example: Ethernet cable break). After each 
RTC4 command, eth_get_last_error can be used to 
check whether an error has occurred during 
communication with the RTC4 Ethernet Board. 
Automatic Ethernet Link Loss detection can be 
enabled by eth_link_loss_config. An 
Ethernet Link Loss usually occurs when the physical 
connection between the RTC4 Ethernet Board and 
the directly connected network device is actually 
broken (for example, cable break, loose contact). If 
automatic Ethernet Link Loss detection is enabled 
(eth_link_loss_config( Mode = 1)), list processing is 
stopped and the laser is switched off immediately 
after an Ethernet Link Loss (similar to 
stop_execution). Automatic 
Ethernet Link Loss detection is especially useful to 
monitor the status of direct connections and to be 
able to configure an appropriate emergency 
shutdown. 
If the check of the physical connection is not 
sufficient (for example, because the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board is only indirectly connected via a network 
switch), active monitoring 
(“watchdog” functionality) can be enabled as an 
alternative. It is enabled by 
eth_watchdog_timer_config and with its 
parameter timer_ms the “watchdog” timer value (in 
ms) is set on the RTC4 Ethernet Board. The 
“watchdog” timer counts down from the set time to 
0 (if it is not reset by eth_watchdog_timer_reset 
before). At 0, stop_execution is executed (= the list 
processing is stopped automatically and the laser is 
switched off immediately). Thus, a connection break 
between PC and RTC4 Ethernet Board within the set 
time frame is recognized on the RTC4 Ethernet Board 
and list processing is aborted immediately as a result. 
When choosing the “watchdog” timer value 
(= timer_ms), take into account that MS Windows 
delays eth_watchdog_timer_reset execution if, for 
example, programs or hardware drivers with higher 
priority are running.

[p.267]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
16 Appendix A: RTC4 Ethernet Board 
267
innovators for industry
16.7 Safe Startup and Shutdown 
Sequences (for Using Control 
Software)
To assure safety during startup, switch on the 
components of the laser system in the following 
order:
(1) Switch on the network PC.
(2) Switch on the power supply for the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board.
(3) Start the control software.
(4) Switch on any required peripheral devices.
(5) Switch on the power supply for the scan system.
(6) Switch on the laser. 
To assure safety during shutdown, switch off the 
components of the laser system in exactly the reverse 
order:
(1) Switch off the laser.
(2) Switch off the power supply for the scan system.
(3) Switch off the peripheral devices.
(4) Terminate the control software. 
(5) Switch off the power supply for the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board.
(6) Shut down the network PC. 
Caution!
• When the PC switches on or off, the RTC4 
board’s output levels might briefly fluctuate, 
resulting in unintended changes to 
laser control signals. The above-mentioned 
startup and shutdown sequences must 
therefore be strictly followed. Otherwise, the 
laser might briefly, unexpectedly and 
dangerously switch on.
Caution!
• Always start up the PC and control software 
prior to turning on the scan system. And switch 
the scan system back off prior to shutting down 
the control software and PC. Otherwise, 
unintended scan system motions might occur. 
The laser must always be switched on last and 
switched off first. Otherwise there is the risk 
that the laser beam might be deflected in an 
arbitrary direction.

16.9.2 Compliance with FCC Rules 
– RTC4 Ethernet Board
The RTC4 Ethernet Board has been tested and found 
to comply with the limits for a Class A digital device, 
pursuant to part 15 of the FCC rules.
These limits are designed to provide reasonable 
protection against harmful interference when the 
RTC4 Ethernet Board is operated in a commercial 
environment. The RTC4 Ethernet Board generates, 
uses, and can radiate radio frequency energy and, if 
not installed and used in accordance with this 
manual, may cause harmful interference to radio 
communications. Operation of the RTC4 Ethernet 
Board in a residential area is likely to cause harmful 
interference in which case the user will be required to 
correct the interference at his own expense.

17 Appendix B: Application Note – Helper Functions in C# (and analogously in VB.net) 
272
innovators for industry
17 Appendix B: Application Note – Helper Functions in C# 
(and analogously in VB.net) 
Software developers need to differentiate between 
managed and unmanaged heap in C#. 
This is important for RTC4 commands, which receive 
a to-be-filled string buffer via the parameter list: 
• convert_ip_to_string 
• convert_mac_to_string 
These “helper functions” expect an IntPtr as a pointer 
to a buffer in C#. 
The following example C# source code exemplifies 
the usage of helper functions. 
The code must be included in a user program. 
UInt32 ip = RTC4ethWrap.get_ip_address(1); 
Int64 mac = RTC4ethWrap.get_mac_address(1);
// To reserve 18 bytes on the unmanaged heap 
// for Mac and IP 
IntPtr s = Marshal.AllocHGlobal(18); 
RTC4ethWrap.convert_ip_to_string(ip, s); 
console.WriteLine("IP is {0}.", 
Marshal.PtrToStringAnsi(s));
RTC4ethWrap.convert_mac_to_string(mac, s); 
Console.WriteLine("mac is {0}.", 
Marshal.PtrToStringAnsi(s)); 
Marshal.FreeHGlobal(s); 
Notes 
• The approach described here is similar in VB.net.

[p.273]

18 Appendix C: iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands and Signals Transmitted to RTC Control Boards 
273
innovators for industry
18 Appendix C: iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands 
and Signals Transmitted to RTC Control Boards
• For usage, see control_command. 
• Example: 
control_command(  data = 0501H ) 
that is, CodeHIGH = 05 (SetMode) and 
CodeLOW = 01 requests that the 
iDRIVE scan system should change the data type 
to be transmitted to “actual position”. The 
iDRIVE scan system evaluates the request and – if 
successful – subsequently transmits the 
“actual position” to the RTC-control board 
(notation in this manual is “Signal 0501H“ in this 
case). 
• The following reference is used in several 
RTC manuals and is thus generic. 
CodeHIGH 
(hex) 
05 
SetMode 
SetMode selects the data signal to be returned from the scan system for the specified axis. 
See also Chapter 8.1.2, “Configuring the Data Signal Transmission Behavior of the Scan System”, 
Page 233. 
Each CodeLOW parameter value corresponds to a particular data type. 
Default setting: CodeLOW = 00H (XY2-100 status word). 
See also “On SetMode”, Page 1204. 
See also “On SetMode, SetControlDefinitionMode and SetEchoMode”, Page 1204. 
iDRIVE scan systems with XY2-100 interface transmit a signed 16-bit-value. 
iDRIVE scan systems with SL2-100 interface transmit an signed 20-bit value. For example, 
excelliSCAN-scan heads. 
iDRIVE scan systems with XY2-100 Enhanced interface transmit a signed 16-bit-value. With 
these, the XY2-100 Converter (Accessory) converts (by multiplying by 16) the value to a 
signed 20-bit value. 
In this document: 
0500H; 0501H; 0502H; 0503H; 0504H; 0505H; 0506H; 0507H; 0508H; 0509H; 0510H; 0511H; 
0512H; 0513H; 0514H; 0515H; 0516H; 0517H; 0518H; 0519H; 051AH; 051BH; 051CH; 051DH; 
051EH; 051FH; 0520H; 0521H; 0522H; 0523H; 0524H; 0525H; 0526H; 0527H; 0528H; 0529H; 
052AH; 052BH; 052CH; 052DH; 052EH; 052FH; 0530H; 0531H; 0532H; 0533H; 0534H; 0535H; 
0536H; 0537H; 0538H; 0539H; 053AH; 053BH; 053CH; 053DH; 053EH; 053FH; 0549H; 055EH;

innovators for industry
CodeHIGH 
(hex) 
12 
As of scan system firmware 2072. 
SetPositionScale 
SetPositionScale causes the scan system to switch to a certain scaling factor. The scan system 
servo electronics multiplies the actual position values received from the RTC-control board by 
this scaling factor. The actual position values sent back to the RTC-control board by the 
scan system are automatically divided by the same scaling factor. In this way, set position and 
actual position are always scaled to match each other. Important: You cannot detect a 
scaling factor ≠ 1 by comparing set position and actual position. 
See also Chapter 8.1.7, “Configuring the Effective Calibration”, Page 242. 
Important: The scaling factor needs to be changed in 2 steps: 1. Execute SetPositionScale with 
CodeLOW = 83H. 2. Execute SetPositionScale with CodeLOW = [00H…03H] (= the desired 
scaling factor). See also “On SetPositionScale”, Page 1205. 
As of scan system firmware 5050. 
Only SCANahead systems: 
SCANahead systems do not support SetPositionScale. With SCANahead systems, the effective 
calibration cannot be changed. 
CodeLOW 
(hex) 
00 
The scaling factor is set to the value 1/1 (= no scaling; default setting) 
01 
The scaling factor is set to the value 1/2 
02 
The scaling factor is set to the value 1/4 
03 
The scaling factor is set to the value 1/8 
83 
Make ready for scaling factor change. 
Notice! Generic information. May be incomplete or even incorrect for your scan system. 
Always consult the dedicated scan system manual!

Store/RestoreTransmissionMode 
Store/RestoreTransmissionMode causes with CodeLOW = FFH the scan system to cache the 
data type currently selected for transmission. It can be reinstated at a later time then with 
CodeLOW = 00H. 
See also Data = 0527H. 
See also “On Store/RestoreTransmissionMode”, Page 1205.

(hex) 
FF 
Store temporarily 
00 
Reinstate

As of scan system firmware 2078. 
SetEchoMode 
SetEchoMode verifies whether data transfer is intact. 
See also Chapter 8.1.9, “Fault Diagnosis and Functional Test”, Page 243. 
SetEchoMode passes an 8-bit value to the scan system with CodeLOW. As a consequence, the 
scan system transmits a 16-bit value (16-bit protocol) or 20-bit value (20-bit protocol) on the 
corresponding status channel to the RTC-control board. If the data transmission has been error-
free, with this: 
• The upper 8 bits and CodeLOW are identical 
• With the 16-bit value, the lower 8 bits / with the 20-bit value, the next lower 
8 bits and the complementary value of CodeLOW (NOT CodeLOW) are identical 
Example with 16-bit protocol: For control_command(1, 1, 0x210A) and if data transfer is error-
free, (get_value(1) AND 0xFFFF) returns 0x0AF5. 
Example with 20-bit protocol: For control_command(1, 1, 0x210A) and if data transfer is error-
free, (get_value(1) AND 0xFFFF0) returns 0x0AF50. 
See also “On SetMode, SetControlDefinitionMode and SetEchoMode”, Page 1204. 
Notice! Generic information. May be incomplete or even incorrect for your scan system. 
Always consult the dedicated scan system manual!

CodeLOW 
(hex) 
 
0N 
Sets Return Channel Multiplexing block length to N+1 
that is, highest Return Channel Multiplexing index = N. In other words: number of 
Return Channel Multiplexing values the iDRIVE scan system has to transmit. 
Allowed values: 1; 2; 3; 4; 6; 8; 12; 16 (= integer divisor of 192 16). 
8N 
Sets the next to-be-configured Return Channel Multiplexing index to N. 
In other words: Defines the position where the signal is transmitted.

innovators for industry
Comments (RTC4) 
• The scan system firmware a.bb.c is read as abbc, 
for example, 5100 corresponds to version 5.10.0, 
and 5054 to version 5.05.4. 
• On SetMode, SetControlDefinitionMode and 
SetEchoMode 
– The data type selected by control_command 
(CodeHIGH = 05H, 0EH oder 21H) is transmitted 
by the scan system until another data type is 
selected. 
– Data returned from the scan system to the 
RTC-control board can be queried by 
get_value, set_trigger or get_waveform. 
Switching to a different data source causes a 
short (serial transmission-related) delay before 
transmission of the first data. Therefore, wait at 
least 50 µs before reading the data.
– After a reset or power-up, it can take around 5 
seconds for data to be returned from the 
scan system, see also get_head_status. After a 
reset or power-up of the scan system, always 
the XY2-100 status word is returned. This 
XY2-100 status word can also be queried by 
get_head_status.
• On SetMode 
– During a temporary error state after the 
maximum allowed temperature was exceeded 
(flag Bit #7 = 0), the scan head’s output stages 
of the affected axis are at least temporarily 
deactivated. The scan system returns to normal 
operation as soon as the temperature 
drops again below the maximum allowed 
temperature.
– If a critical error occurs (flag Bit #9 = 0), the 
scan system automatically enters a permanent 
error state, in which the output stages of the 
affected axis remain deactivated – even if the 
critical error was only temporarily present. 
Normal operation is not resumed. Flag Bit #9 is 
only reset by a hardware reset. Critical errors 
are for instance improper internal voltages 
(flag Bit #13 = 0), external power supply 
interruption (flag Bit #8 = 0) or reaching a 
critical edge position (flag Bit #5 = 0).
– During both temporary and permanent error 
states, the scan system continues to transmit 
data to the RTC-control board. Even in these 
states, switching or selection of data signals for 
diagnostic purposes is still possible.
– The flags indicate the scan system’s operational 
state. The scan module can return one of two 
flag blocks indicating the current operational 
state (data = 0528H, 0529H) or alternatively 
one of two further flag blocks indicating the 
operational state at the moment of the most 
recently occurred operation interruption (data 
= 052BH, 052CH). After every successful restart 
– and, as long as no error has occurred – all 
status informations of the two latter blocks 
(data = 052BH, 052CH) are irrelevant. Only, as 
soon as an error causes a switch into a 
temporary or permanent error state, the 
current status values are saved into these two 
blocks. In this case, also an event code is 
simultaneously set, indicating which particular 
event caused the error state. This event code 
can be read out separately (data = 052AH).
– The angle bit-values (actual position, 
set position, position error) or angle bit/ms-
values (actual speed) returned to the RTC4 can 
be converted into °-values or °/ms-values by the 
scan system’s calibration angle. The calibration 
angle can be read out by data = 0523H.
– intelliWELD scan systems can be supplied with 
various number of sensors. Reference the 
scan system manual. This manual lists the 
command codes for all its theoretically possible 
sensors.

[p.315]
RTC4 Manual 
Doc. Rev. 1.9.1 en-US 
18 Appendix C: iDRIVE Scan Systems - Control Commands and Signals Transmitted to RTC Control Boards 
315
innovators for industry
• On SetPositionScale 
– If the scaling factor for scaling the position 
values is changed, then the user program’s 
calibration factor for calculating RTC4 control 
values (in bits) from the desired Image Field 
position values (in mm) needs to be subjected 
to an inverse proportional scaling, 
see Chapter 4.4, “Image Field Size”, Page 45. 
In addition, the jump and mark speed should 
be adjusted.
– The currently set scaling factor can be queried 
with data = 053FH.
• On SetPosAcknowledgeLevel 
– The default start behavior is for the scan system 
to set the limit value to B7H after every power-
up or reset. If other limit values are desired, 
they must be separately set for each axis 
(CodeHIGH = 15H). SCANLAB recommends 
setting only limit values (CodeLOW) > 14H (that 
is, 20 counts or 0.03% of 216 counts). Lower 
values can lead to frequent system safety 
shutdowns due to Position Acknowledge time 
outs (set position not reached for an excessive 
time).
• On Store/RestoreTransmissionMode 
– Store/RestoreTransmissionMode has no 
effect if a power-up or reset was executed after 
the most recent execution of the 
Store/RestoreTransmissionMode (data 
= 17FFH).
